And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries next to the large one on the stomach, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a line-by-line translation of the medieval medical text about the treatment of hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and they have been treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not improve, then perform cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is located entirely outside, below a pointed dimple, and I cautery below the two holes; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then perform a large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and I another on the liver, and I another on the spleen for the entire claw-shaped cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, keep it at rest until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut thelul (a term for fleshiness), heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut thelul; and leave your hand in that position until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there are many theluls, cauterize each one as we have said; after that cure them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchemy (possibly meaning a chemical substance), it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then comes a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 If anyone has a fistula and it is inflamed, and produces pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe it with a thin probe and make sure you know the depth of the entire probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 Afterwards, heat the cautery that looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the corrupt and putrid flesh is burned away, once or two or three times, depending on how much is needed; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the fistula reaches the body of the bladder and intestines, be careful in those areas and do not perform this procedure except on solid tissue, and keep in mind that it is not always possible; after resting the area until it is healed, if the wound is closed and the contents have been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is fully healed; but if the contents are not removed, know that the wound is infected and the bone has become corrupt; and such cases will be discussed in their proper place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the cold comes to the kidneys, and there is swelling from an abundance of wind, and they have no desire for a woman, then you should perform cautery on the kidneys, one on each side, using the clavicle cautery that we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cautery on the outer side above the bladder, where the hair of the groin starts, with one on the right and one on the left, each cauterization should be as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be shaped as described before.

Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	In this context, "de la hainche" likely refers to a condition known as dropsy or edema in modern medicine. It is characterized by the accumulation of fluid in the body cavities or tissues. In Old French, "hainche" can refer to swelling or inflammation, and it was often treated with cauterization in medieval medical texts. Here's a possible translation:
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humorous vapors descend to the hip's case, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one of the signs is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip's case with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the case as it turns, so that the case is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olive size, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip's case, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterwards, perform cautery; and the methods of cautery are of two kinds: namely, hot irons and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 The fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: cauterize the boil with three triangular irons in this shape, making a deep and large wound between each iron spaced the width of a thumb, and make the irons olive-shaped; sometimes a single iron is used in the middle of the boil, resulting in four as per this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the method used for sciatica, when pain persists only in the hip and does not reach either the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it comes down to the thigh and leg, perform two fire cauteries where the patient indicates the pain lies, and four cauteries above the ankle on the inner side; let the cautery be knife-like, and let the thickened part of the flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize it there where they feel the pain three or four times with the "points" cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, perform more cauterization; and if the patient feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long such that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen several who performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it for so long that the leg swelled up completely, as did the foot, and the entire foot became pierced and rotten.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a surgery of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two joints together, perform cautery on one and then the other, in the following way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise men said in the cautery for edema, this is the method, make such an iron and let its head be as thick as a thumb's width, or slightly less, and let it be interlaced, and let there be a space between each interlace equal to the width of a bean; and let the interlaces be reversed in two parts, and let them be like knots, and have one well-made iron handle; and this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery because of fear of its effect, and if one were to see those who use it; and nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries which can be endured by those on whom it is used, and where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of medical fire is that you make an interlaced tool where the edge of the opening descends, and let it be made of copper or iron with one side long, and in its height have two nodes, and let there be a space between each equal to the width of a finger; and let them be open above and below, and come together in this shape.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Afterward, place the box of the hip on the patient lying on a healthy, nearby side, and then press firmly with your hand on the box of the hip; after that, pour between the two circles of the hourglass hot water that has been heated over fire one time, and let it stay for an hour according to the time, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For there is found a biting/stinging sensation just like from fire; and when the biting/stinging sensation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and gently raise the hip away from the hot water, and leave it in this way for three days, and apply butter until the blackened area from the burn is removed; and let it be left alone for three days so that any dead tissue can come out; and this would be the final assistance after the treatment of poultices until it has healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has extended to the thigh or the leg, make an instrument that matches what you have done in the hip enlargement; and this is the manner of hot cautery, which I have written in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take alkali and quicklime, equal parts of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 so that it has a small hole in the upper part where the tip of a razor can enter; and place another pot well soldered on top of it, and put hot cautery, soft, on top of alkali and quicklime until there are two fingers' breadths of powder above what you have smeared with your hand; and leave it like that until the hot cautery becomes lukewarm and solid in the pot soldered on top, then take all of the hot cautery and throw it back on the alkali and quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very weak and is refreshed with deeds of medical work and with cauteries of other limbs. For it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes well inflammation, such as tetanus and melegaeta (a type of tree resin) and chalk with soap, all mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure in which a man was cured of the pain of inflammation and sciatic nerve, and he praised it highly, and said that no other cure was done, and that he was cured at once when this cure was performed, and he bathed as is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this way that you take of white lead (another name for litharge) fresh and dry, and grind it well with a little bit of fat, and place it on the inflammation and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain resides, and bind it; and leave it on for three hours and by the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly heated, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will completely go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a fire cautery unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the depression that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called foscile.[Observation: The translation of "foscile" as another toe is an educated guess. However, I am not entirely sure about this, because there isn't enough context provided for a clear understanding of what this term refers to.]
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat's dung, heat it on fire until it becomes coals, and place it on wool, leaving it until it becomes ashes; and repeat this process, not stopping until you think that it will reach the swelling and that the pain has ceased; and this method of cautery is called "cautery of goat.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from percussion, or from excessive evacuation, or from spread out cold matter, none of these instances is suitable for cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or other similar things, three lines be signed on the back, in the place where the pain resides, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauterizations or more, according to the potency and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterization be done using the type of cauterization called "poins"; and if you wish, do three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien method, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find on the back, on the last spine of the spine, an appearance which comes before the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this sort, in this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery, making two or three lines and having the points close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 Afterwards, heal the area until it is healed as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to a gouty area that is in the sinew's marrow.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which is properly called "gout" by laymen, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, it can be cured by cauteries in the following way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary that you touch the sole of the foot, if you perform cautery on the entire sole as one calls it "puncture".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, perform cautery on each knee three or four times on every part, with the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand away for too long that the flesh does not burn.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there is still pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you treat it well and purge phlegm, it will heal with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of an abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the haunches and this is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that evacuate the belly, so that feces descends from their stomach; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has subsided, and then massage it with your fingers, and apply a bandage below the abscess over the bone of the wrist, and in such a way that it forms half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is made:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and excretes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then return the intestines to their place; and have the assistant place his hand so that they do not move back; work well on the patient's thighs, and put a cushion and a sheet underneath them, and another on the chest to hold the hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your entire hand, holding it directly and firmly until you reach the bone; if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you do so; pay attention that the intestines do not protrude while performing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer further harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine according to the measure of eggs, and for adults also as large according to their measure; after three days cure the wound of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left long enough, so that the boils do not come out when he moves around in the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and let him wear it for forty more days; and have good rest, that he not exert himself too much and be wary of excessive consumption of food and drink, and loud talking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	"of abdominal surgery" is what you meant to say, right? The Old French phrase "la routure dou ventre" translates to "the rupture/tear of the belly/stomach".
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform the fire cautery of the returning cautery according to its quantity, and let one third of the intestine be burnt; then cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the location of the rupture and make a line above it according to its width, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cautery claw.[addcontext] The text describes the use of cauterization (burning) as a medical treatment for ruptures in the stomach or abdomen. The instructions involve marking the location of the rupture and making lines above and below it according to its width, before placing the hand in the middle of the cautery tool (claw-shaped). It's important to note that this is a medieval medical text and some of the practices described may not be considered acceptable or effective by modern medical standards.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and subtler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some member (limb)
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or being injured, and this pain lasts for a long time and the cures of medicine are ineffective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "pointed" cautery, and the cautery should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, as well as its location and the degree of its turning and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for it is customary that it must change on the limb that is close to it, therefore you should continue with the cauteries until the patient heals.
de meselerie	of leprosy (Hansen's disease)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The eyebrows are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 If you wish to cauterize the eyes, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not subside or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then perform the V cauteries on the head: I in the middle of the forehead, and the other towards the front at the end of the hairs; and II on the two horns (temples), and one behind on the back of the head; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and long enough for the scabs to come out, allowing the vapors of the foul humors to escape; and cauterize the eye according to what it presents.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are at the back pressing down, so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do with cautery, the more help I provide, and movement increases its benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.[Note: "ways of iron" likely refers to different types of cauterizing irons]
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After the cure, sprinkle the wound with flour of vetch and honey and other cures until it is healed.[Note: "flour of vetch" is likely a medicinal powder made from the Vicia sativa plant][
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterize the member according to its size; and let the cautery be slightly into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes, cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and in this way, swelling is removed; but no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	The term "de albaras" does not appear in the provided Old French medical text. It is possible that this is a transcription error or it may be a term from a different source. Without more context, it is not possible to provide a translation or interpretation of "de albaras".
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become persistent and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and each one part of swallows' blood and sparrows' blood; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The phrase "li cure de chancre par cautere" can be translated as "the treatment of chancre by cautery". Chancre was a term used in medieval medicine to refer to various types of ulcers or sores, including those associated with syphilis. Cautery was one method of treating these sores, and involved using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn the affected area. This was believed to promote healing by destroying infected tissue and sealing off blood vessels. The specific instructions for performing such a treatment would depend on the particular medical text and context in which it appears.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a chancre first appears and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet, physicians say that one should also perform cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before; and a more appropriate thing is for it to be cauterized around the edge with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in killing or due to the excess it makes, or due to the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like that afterwards.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 because it will hasten in dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the gangrene is alleviated.[note]I'm not completely sure about the translation of "le cours de la porriture soit alegis". I assume it means something like "the progression of the gangrene is alleviated/lessened", but I'm not certain. This is also the case for some other parts of the text, such as "adubelati" and "le chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor". These are all translations that make sense to me based on context, but I can't be certain without more information.[/note] ​
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the care until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of illness exists, which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a consumption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate the application of fire cautery, then heat the pointed and broad cautery instruments slightly or intensely, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all the corruption, leaving nothing behind, so that all that is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days and apply ground-up cautery instruments on the cauterized places with oil until the burns from the fire and all the corruption are removed.[OP note: "ground-up cautery instruments" is a translation of "soffre broiet", which literally means "broken support" or "support that has been broken down". I interpreted it as referring to the remains of the cauterized instruments used in the previous step, which have now been ground up into smaller pieces. The Old French term could potentially be interpreted differently based on context.]
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of wound-healing plasters.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy flesh has not grown, that is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to the remaining unhealed and corrupt areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this abscess has sometimes been healed with a medicinal poultice instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is more effective. I have already mentioned the treatment for medicinal poultices in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the splinters that come to (or go into) the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that in the feet, due to insufficient care, arises a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swelling that wounds the foot.[It might be helpful to know that "defuers" here means neglect or lack of care, "blesce" means wound, and "piet" means foot.]
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, the fire cautery, and the cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 The fire cautery is: heat the cauterizing iron as if it were a roof tile, and make sure it is made of good metal and of a size that can surround the nail completely, with thin edges. Then place it while still hot on the nail and keep your hand wrapped all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; leave it in this position for three days until it begins to putrefy. Afterwards, apply a plaster made from crushed mallows with oil, and leave it on overnight; the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure the wound with a compress soaking it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are corrupted by humors within the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply a hot water cautery; and it is done in the following way: take an iron or copper rod, or a pen of vaulted stone, and place it on the nail and the stylet, that is to say, pumice stones; and place the rod so that it surrounds entirely, then put some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, pressing your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the base of the nail, allowing the hot water to find a deep path up to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will detach completely along with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 In this way, do one after another, until you reach all those that are in the body, then cure the inflammations that cause flesh growth.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking/trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should apply four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the hip, and one on the stomach at the location of the olive cautery; this will stop the shaking, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes it happens that the body appears covered in bathed wounds or foul-smelling pustules, which come from large corrupt materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 When they first appear, it is necessary to apply a cautery to each chief of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from a myrtle wood stick, with its tip taken by fire, or from an aristolochia root that is long enough, or from a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow anymore, but the superfluities from which they come are broken, and they heal; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut[The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery which has been cut in a wound or incision of an abscess or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez. Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the stopping of the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help then it is of no use.[Note: This sentence is a continuation of the previous translation and provides a cautionary statement about the methods mentioned in the previous sentence.]
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who does not have medical equipment or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and pull hard until it stays above the wound and vein; and he should not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what he needs in terms of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgeries.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or heated medicine, and we have described their causes, instruments, and forms; and I put this chapter about the head down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter the same way so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come to be healed.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There come those who are so fond of their illness that they would easily die from the severity and greatness of its grip, and one should fear for these people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are some who pretend to be healed and say "wait, I am cured," yet their illness is contemptuous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not appropriate to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than into your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open for those whom you are certain and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the care of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you establish good reputation, glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inhale the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	"the head full of water" or "the swollen head"
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	"Know that this disease often occurs in children during childbirth, and when the birth is difficult and the mother grips the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason."
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	"And I have never seen this disease except in children, and among those that I have seen, their deaths came quickly; and for this reason it seems better to me to leave such work to more skilled practitioners."
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	"And I saw a child whose head was full of water and became larger every day until it could no longer support its own weight; and the fluid increased so much that he died, and this fluid collects under the bone at the temple, between the brain and the skull; and the procedure is such when the fluid is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the head, a slit wide enough for the fluid to flow out; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the fluid can escape; and here is the shape of the spatula:"
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more advanced and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, following this pattern:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the mouth are open on both sides, and pus comes out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond (to treatment); then you must make three incisions in the middle of the chin, following this pattern:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the pus.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Afterwards, bind the wounds with bandages and powder, and apply wine and oil, leaving it like this for five days; then undo it, and treat the wound with dressings and ointments, and leave it bound as well, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe where the swelling of the abscess is most prominent, and where the pus has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then at the place where the abscess is open, and the filling of water, and the opening according to what you have the power; and take care not to cut the artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the outpouring of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	The term "de reume" is not present in the provided text. However, based on context clues and an understanding of medieval medical terminology, it is likely that "reume" refers to "rheum," or an abnormal bodily discharge, often associated with illness.

Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood jumps up continually outside.
