se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if pustules appear, let the eye be unbound before the seventh day, and apply a compress of that which soothes a pustule; and when it has calmed, then unbind the vision and place upon its face a covering to protect for some days, and let it always remain in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then go out of the house little by little and return to your duties; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And there came to us someone who was from Yrach (Iraq), who told us that in their country they make almagda perciet, which one sucks the water (from), but nonetheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see them; and they should be made of pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the tops of them be of the same delicacy, and the backs in three sharp angles.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/auge)
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes various kinds of warts are born, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such warts that have hardened flesh of a fox-colored hue, and such that have soft flesh of good color.[Note: The translation of "fuxe" as "fox-colored" is an educated guess based on the context. A more literal translation would be "speckled"]
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then in the case of such a joint that is not swollen, but is only dislocated, you should make the patient sit between your hands with their face towards the sun; clear their nostrils and apply a leech to those parts and draw it out; then remove as much as you can hold with a thin, sharp spatula on one side, until you are certain that the part is completely free.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut, you should open it with all the very fine and light instruments, leaving nothing behind; and if pus forms, or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are harmful abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all growths are removed, then pour wine or vinegar on the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nostril does not open and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if the moisture does not flow out as it should, know that there is a thickening in the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut: then you must insert a moderately thick linen thread, tied with thin threads at intervals of about half a finger's breadth; and place the patient's nose in the snow if possible, and draw the end of the thread through the nostril until it comes out of the mouth; and children do this often in school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head that comes through the snow with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and feel which of the threads are wet.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this to know that the maggots have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the filth, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nostril as before; do this three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all remaining flesh; and then place a piece of willow bark on the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, such as a reed; and the conduit should also be similar; and if you wish, make a closed reed; and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose, called "telul," which grows and becomes large to the point that it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then place the cautery or hot medicine on it; and if it is delayed until it has grown large, be careful if it is hard, of a dark color, and with little sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty the patient's nose and cut it carefully without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two edges together with a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the edges are separated on one side and the other, then you must burn all the flesh around them until they heal, then bring the two edges together with a stitch and hold them, and put powdered dragon's blood and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or any other adhesive plaster on top of it, and leave it on until it dries out, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you approximate the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses, similar to grains of pepper, sometimes smaller and sometimes larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut in each part; then apply the place after the incision of powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then clean the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling of the flesh of the gums arises, which the ancients called "albulus"; then you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of "sordens" (a medical term used in medieval texts) - It is possible that this refers to a specific medical condition, but I am unable to find a precise definition or translation for it with the context provided. "Sordes" can be translated as "filth", "dirt", or "crusts" in a general medical context.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, accumulations occur on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, greenish, and gray, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you should have the patient sit between your hands, and their chin in your holy hand, and clean the visible teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first cleaning, it is good; if not, then resume again on the second day and the third, until everything is cleaned; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the task requires, because the scrapers used to clean above the teeth have different forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as much as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very risky substance up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is forced to evacuate, you must make sure that the tooth is loose.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is a toothache, and they have a bad tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, as we have often seen done by these surgeons; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, then you should cauterize around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides; then pull it out with your hands or with fine tweezers at the first root and root, until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the tweezers; and have the patient's head in your lap, holding it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After pulling the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with cloth where the holes are; and then gently tighten it with pliers, so as not to break it when tightening; and you must carefully perform bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, for if the root is left, it will cause greater pain for the patient when returning.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act as some ignorant healers do, who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break the root and do not bring about what we have described, but rather sometimes cause great illness due to the remaining roots or the broken root, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply a mixture of vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize the area.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to move teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick stock so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be made of well-forged iron, and should have teeth to hold onto [the tooth].
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains to be pulled, you should place cotton soaked in butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the place is softened, then apply tongs called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and inside they should be made like a file, and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tongs, you must expose all the flesh around the root and place the instrument called "althali" there, that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[translated] \_/ | | | | | | | | | | | | |
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which forms are described hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument that has two hooks, of which the form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other metallic instruments that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which the form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments that are not mentioned here. And the wise master skillfully finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness indicate, for there are such diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients due to their diversity of use. And one does not break anything on the cart or other bones, but rather searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have said, and helps with gestures; of which the forms are as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but rather can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, it heals with this entire instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and similarly in young women, you should know if the tooth is not erupted after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; and if it is opposite to the tooth, take this instrument, which has the shape of a small beak, and made of sharp iron at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And frequently take the file and hold it between your fingers for several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a file like this as shown in the figure.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similar to the file used for making needles; and with this file, you should file the tooth frequently, several days, lightly so that it does not move until it becomes loose; then use a smooth plane at the end in order to even it out completely, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, then you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth loosen, either from being knocked out or from falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail, then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the patient's teeth on top of the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering until you reach the starting point, and pull your hand gently but firmly, so that the teeth do not move at all; and let the thread be tied to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaws with a thread using pincers, and align them, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose one, and position it so as not to cut the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then tie it with another thread; let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the form of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the empty socket, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue, which one is born with, or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your hand, and lift their tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage, and if there is hardness or knot, which comes from a healed wound, then insert the hook and cut wide this ligament; and make sure that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is beneath; and when you have done so, apply a compress of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue; and have the patient change it every night, so that the ligament does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if there is bleeding, put vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a ligature cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, throw the "oncine" (a type of surgical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood overwhelms your work, put vitriol powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you pull everything out; then lift it up with ease and support, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes abscesses called "godath" come inside the throat, and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and bluish color, do not touch them at all with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it at all with iron, to avoid bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will remove it, or it will break open by itself; and if it has a whitish color and thin roots, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check whether the hard abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open their mouth and take the surgical instrument in your hands, and press down the tongue with it, covering all the instrument; it should be made of thin silver or bronze, as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you have pressed the tongue down beneath the entire instrument and you see the abscess, take the "oncine" (a type of surgical instrument) and insert it into the almond (growth), and pull it out as much as you can; and pull some of the pus with it, then cover the wound with the instrument, which is shaped like a pair of forceps. But be aware that the patient's teeth are clenched together, and one presses against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of hard iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other side; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision rinse the patient's throat with warm water, and vinegar, and salt, and if there is bleeding, then rinse the patient's throat with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say a small abscess; and she had tightly closed her entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passage, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in that state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two teeth through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened then soon and stuck an instrument into one of the wounds, then pulled it out and extracted a large piece of bow; then I put another piece in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I stuck the instrument into these abscesses, and cut out a part, and only a little blood came out; and so the conduit of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess increased again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I tied it off and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the wetness descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the abscess has calmed down and it is fine, then you should lance it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is blood-red or the color of pus or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the appearance and length as I have said, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and lance it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you should not cover up the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cover up more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being covered (i.e. having a bandage or dressing applied), you should use strategy/cunning in performing the cauterization while alleviating their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of the cautery is hot heat (or "fire", as in the original French text).
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let the patient place their head in your lap, and then press their tongue to the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with living hot water (i.e. boiled water), so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use this instrument, whose shape is as follows:[It seems like there is a missing description or image of the instrument being referred to here.]
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair on the head where the medicine is placed, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the bites of the medicine have calmed down; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument full of cotton into the wound, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to renew the cautery with the medicine, then renew it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton stuffed with butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and cured with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put them in a pot and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And whether it be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes be put into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes mortified; then begin again frequently, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless the abscess has cooled down.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell filled with it in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with being healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or a fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press down on the patient's tongue with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit, so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of napkin, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument made of reed in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, that he does not choke, or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient pushes the instrument in themselves, so that they know where the object is located; and move it up and down until the object comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat's fat or flesh.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the veins are medicated, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the tapeworm, draw it out with a tiny hook or delicate pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that is not effective, take a live dog's tail and put it down the patient's throat, then apply a hot iron to the end of the tail, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And make sure the patient drinks only water all day.[NOTE: This translation is based on the assumption that "teigne" is being used as a verb in this context, which means "to make drink". If it is being used as an adjective meaning "afflicted with lice", then the translation would be "And let the afflicted patient bathe in water all day."]
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full glass of cold water and open the patient's mouth, pour it in slowly without causing them to choke, and move it around with your hand frequently; and as soon as the tapeworm senses the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot with hot coals in it, and cover it with a pierced cloth, with the hole of the instrument in the middle; then place your fumigation in it and have the patient hold the handle of the instrument in their mouth, closing their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but rather reaches the sinuses; the sinus will soon fall out, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation several times; make the patient endure thirst, eating only salty and bitter foods and drinking no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the vein, it is when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers so that they can enter into the throat; and it should look like a bird's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its form: [It is possible that this sentence refers to an illustration of the instrument that has not been provided.]
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many similarities of abscesses exist, according to what remembrance comes after this in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its very form, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different from those of the belly, and abscesses in fleshy parts are different from those that come in joints, and each should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such kind that must be pierced when they are grown and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are next to joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses appear near joints, and are left until they rot around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupt, which causes constriction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the perforation until it has died, it will harm the main member; or it is near the foundation, then one should pierce it as soon as it has died; and one must not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion completed, except for one that is near the foundation, lest it rots inside and forms a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member.[Note: This sentence seems incomplete or out of context, but I've translated it as literally as possible.]
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fatty place, it is better to leave the puncture until it is firm after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be prolonged, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.[](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Et%20si%20a%20aucun%20aposteme%20que%20sont%20perciet%20selonc%20le%20large%20dou%20cors,%20selonc%20ceu%20que%20li%20membres%20en%20ait%20mestier.)
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the ear, and cover; when it has become as a cloth, and is mortified, then one must do similarly as for boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such where one cuts in the shape of a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of shins; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, then do not pull out all the pus in that hour, but pull out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then pull out some more; do this many times, increasing in size, until all the pus has come out; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit (breath) suddenly jumps with the issue of the breath, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a wide incision, then apply soft bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses with many holes, then you must insert a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin, and you have sewn it around, then you must fill it with soft cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and fresh water, wet a cloth, and apply it to the wound frequently.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in light hands as described in this book. If it is winter and the place where the abscess is located is very sensitive, you should put up tents and wet cloths in hot wine and oil; and if it is summer and the place is fleshy, you should put damp cloths on it in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil until the third day, as we have said. Then loosen the abscess, dry it and treat it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one must proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here begins that chapter.[1](#myfootnote1)
des soros	I believe you are asking for a translation of the word "soros" from Old French. The translation of "soros" in this context is likely "abscesses."
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses of the head come, and are shaped like blisters, similar to the hock of a chicken, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fatty and similar to those with moisture like pimples; and there are others that are hard and rough when cut, and there is no doubt that the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedure for cutting is that you test every instrument called "entromissoire", of which there are various forms, to see what it contains.[Comment: "Entromissoire" appears to be a type of medical tool used in surgery. The text instructs the practitioner to check or test each such tool before use.]
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, then they open it from above the long [part].[Comment: The text seems to be saying that if a surgical instrument is found to contain moisture, one should make an incision on the top of the affected area rather than somewhere else.[Note: It's possible that "lonc" in this context refers to the length of the incision or cut, but without additional context it's difficult to say for certain.]
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, scrape the skin without leaving any of the membrane that contains the moisture, for it comes back if anything is left; then soak a cotton swab in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and those who stay overnight will take care of it.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are certain that none remains overnight; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess contains yellow pus, cut it in this manner, longwise; and insert your fingers, and scrape it all around, and make sure to drain all the pus that is inside; and if an artery resists, do what I have told you before.[Brainsize_ai]
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly for the abscess if it is hard, and to cut and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if some of these abscesses, either on the head or elsewhere, have no moisture, and such was an abscess that I found on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and unable to break; and if one had struck it with anything, it would have caused as much injury as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 And in other abscesses appearing on the head, except for those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, let the incision be as low as possible so that pus may easily exit; and treat them as is appropriate.[It's worth noting that "bowe" here likely refers to purulent matter or discharge coming from an abscess or wound.]
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is not a complete sentence in Old French, but it appears to be referring to scrofula, a form of tuberculosis that affects the lymph nodes in the neck. Here's an example of how you might translate a sentence containing "des scrophules":
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times, these abscesses occur on the neck, and beneath the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and they are large, and are connected to one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each and every scrofula is specifically within its own cavity, just like the knots and abscesses of the head, as we have said, and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are some wicked ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 Therefore, in the one that you see with good disposition when touched, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and moves from every side and is not airy near the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you must cut it open from above, and skin it from each side, and extend the two lips of the wound with sutures if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head. And draw pus and pus, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hands do not slip, and not dig in too deep, so that you do not cut what you should not.[NOTE: I am assuming "si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief" is referring to the previous statement about treating abscesses of the head. If it refers to something else, then please let me know.]
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any drying powders that stop bleeding, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then check with your skill if there are any small nodules left, cut them and clean (the wound).
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the nodule, it should not be cut at its root, but bound with a strong double thread and left to fall without causing harm; then apply old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound and bandage it.['
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire abscess, it is necessary to bring together the two edges of the wound and suture it immediately, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you aim to cut the root of it and pull it out, and then suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For those abscesses that have excess matter, lance it where it is bulging; and lance it in the same way as previously mentioned, by making an incision and then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it drains the remaining corrupt matter; and when the wound is thoroughly cleaned, cure it with ointment and allow flesh to grow until it heals.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" appears to be a misspelling or variation of the French word "esc(h)inance", which is derived from the Latin "scrotum". It refers to the scrotum, the sac that contains the testicles in males.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the "tailleure de la gorge," but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is according to their written words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and this is not done with ease, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed, as is the case when they have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which results from constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphac, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and slender.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat completely, then split the windpipe until it reaches the hyoid bone; and avoid cutting any blood vessels, if you see anything; and then cut the syphac as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the trachea which jumps out through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and stitch it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the breathing has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then place a bandage on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus they are kept from dying; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the cartilage in the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed out of it, and I realized that she had not cut an artery or vein but rather the windpipe was exposed through the wound.[INST) Je apris aucuns vaisseaux de sang et les li ligai; et puis li bailli a boire, si com je pus; et quant ele vit que je ne la voleoit morir, elle commencha a revenir en soi.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that she lost her voice, and later regained consciousness; for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "goiter hernias", and are large abscesses in the color of a lump, and are very common in women; and are according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental (goiter) is according to two manners, one of which resembles fat, and the other manner resembles an abscess coming from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on forcefully except in the one that is small, and test and search the entirety of the inserted (goiter): if you find it like ordinary fat, and it does not bleed through any vein, then cut it, as one cuts fat, and pull out all its covering, if there is any; and search thoroughly, and cure it well until it heals perfectly.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways there are, which I will tell you all the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference which is between abscess and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an "issue" is characterized by heat and fever that persist until the boiling (of pus) has passed and the decay is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
