Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With an abscess there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains a sac (syfac) which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes swollen; and there are two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoires," according to the form that comes in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, so that you know that the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intruder, and be careful that it does not jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs and corrupts, whatever color it has, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come out, know that it is fat, then lance it in a cross shape, and take tongs, and gently scrape from each side and place the cotton where it lies so that you pull it out clean with the linen; and if you cannot pull it out clean, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains, the disease will return many times; and if some remains and the blood bothers you, then apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind it up and place warm, soothing things for abscess on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, then cut the two edges of the wound, and treat what hinders the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if a pulsating vein is contrary to you or another, hasten and use the place of vitriol powder, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound rots, and let the boiling of the blood subside; then return to cover what remains to be covered of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of invasive instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to sew up wounds, and are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and the new ones are better, and are more proven for use with black plumage for encircling the openings of fistula; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the humors are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are humors that have two bumps of three types; and there are humors that have three bumps, and they are also of three types; and there are humors that have two bumps, and humors with a single bump only, and they are of three types; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these (humors) are sharp, and there are some that cut only on one side, which is used to scrape the flesh, so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and of the intromittent ones, needles are placed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scabbard of a fistula, in this shape, to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And they place it sometimes on the wound that bleeds profusely from veins and arteries, and sometimes in this large shape:[img](![scabs of abscesses](https://i.imgur.com/1IWwvuZ.png))
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes, the nipples of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupted, to such an extent that they resemble female breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to the form of this line from b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then remove the fat and fill the wound with medicine made from pork flesh, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if the nipple points downward and is soft due to its large size as often happens in women, make two incisions above in the shape of two similar splits; such that one holds the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line b to g; then remove the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come in the armpits are types of hard scrofulas, some of which contain moisture.[NOTE: Scrofula is a form of tuberculosis that mainly affects the lymph nodes, characterized by the formation of hard, movable swellings.]
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who have an excess of moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment to it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofulous swelling, incise it as we have said in the fissures of scrofulous swellings, and if the wound closes up again, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is damaged and the skin over it is stuck down, swelling often occurs, and the same happens when a vein is engorged and becomes swollen; this can be recognized when the swelling is long and deep, and feels hard to the touch. If it is due to a vein, the swelling will be softer and closer to the surface. It is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is located near joints, under fingernails, in the neck, or in many other places, and can be very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the iron cure and also the one who is at the head should avoid it, and in the one who is swollen with artery fent above the skin; then perform the incision along the edges, and neatly separate the artery from the webs, until it is uncovered; then place underneath it a needle, and make it penetrate to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then pierce the area between the two ties with an intromitter until the blood that is in it comes out, and let the abscess be released; then make the wound heal gradually, so that the ligatures fall; then cure this with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then you must stain your hand with whatever you can of the abscess on all the skin, then place the needle underneath the area you hold with your hand, and make it penetrate, and let there be one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with a ligature of one of two parts on the two sides of the filaments; and if you fear that the threads may come out, then place another needle under all the abscess along the incision of the first needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is tied; then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses can come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses can come to the nerves when they are wounded, or through excessive effort, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and all places where there are joints, namely swellings, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in various dispositions without pain; and when one strongly constricts, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and the one who is in the head or forehead makes the skin suppurate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root;
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and not only there, a disease which is called "fungi" because of its likeness to them, and it has subtle roots and large lumps; and some are small and others very large; and I saw a man who had two such growths in his belly that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were fissured, and moisture was continually running from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six pounds; and the procedure in cutting into them is to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist with fine roots; then cut widely with a spatula, and have the cautery ready with fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For when cutting, there often comes a great loss of blood, and if the blood flow overcomes you, then hasten to the cauterizer; and if you see the patient fearful and terrified of the incision of the iron, take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then bind it, and do not cease binding the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this without causing pain; and if the roots are thick, there is fear of cutting the same due to the belly, but you can easily cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care not to cut the nerve which is of a fleshy color and poor sensation and has a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cauterized wound or split of an abscess, and it is located on the belly and in one of the sides, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the abscess and the opening of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and has an opening with diverse issue.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it rises up and then returns; and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after strenuous activity.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens clearly when you press it with your hand, do not restrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the treatment is to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or the vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 So you must leave the cure alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or boil, you must instruct the patient to expose their throat, lie flat and straight, then tie a bandage around the swelling; then have them lie still in your hands, go around the place you marked with the spatula, extend half of the abscess above the bandage, and place your index finger on it, and feel for the intestine; if you find it caught by the bandage, release it and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find a boil, grab it with the tongs and remove excess fluid; and if an artery or vein opposes you, go around it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and tie them in a cross that you make perforate; then pull the abscess tight on four stitches with the needles, and if you see any pus, remove the needles and leave the place open until it dries up, and let the dead flesh fall out by itself; or cut it when it becomes thin and dry, then treat what needs to be treated, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or fluid you find, then treat the wound and suture it.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is required in its treatment. And the ancients have said that when chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it at all, for no one can ever cure it; nor did anyone cure it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is to first purge the patient of black bile; then make them sweat if they have obvious bloating, then prepare the patient for the procedure with a good rest period; then apply your leeches or plasters to the chancre and remove all hair from around it without leaving any behind; let the blood flow freely, and thoroughly clean the area with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then apply another treatment until it heals completely.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning "eclypses"; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: namely tympanites and hydrops archis, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclypses" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is danger; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus: lift the patient upright in your hands, and have the minister press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the abdomen, then take a blunt instrument such as a small spoon according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pointed, and yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot bleed; then check if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the belly button three fingers wide downwards and below up to the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the belly button three fingers wide; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is necessary that the patient does not lie on the incision so that superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand over the entire abdomen between the skin and the hypochondrium as in flaying to the width of a finger or more; then pierce the hypochondrium until the instrument reaches the visible place, which is the water's location, then remove it and insert the instrument of this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hinge, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the joints are cut like a feather, and that is the shape of the incision that writers cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the collector, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it then sinks down on the instrument; you then empty out half or a third of it, for if you empty out more than is appropriate at that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit through the weapon, or they fall unconscious, or they approach death; but empty it according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulses; then pull the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the cork that stops up the hole which is above the syphon, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring it, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to continue until there is only a little bit of water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye it with drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Not at any time does a child born have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary for him to immediately make a hole with a very thin awl according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place a thin piece of reed in the opening and bind it and keep it like that for 3 or 4 days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose hole is small, let it be medicined with a piece of sponge, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 He who does not have the hole (the meatus) in its place is injured, for some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the tip, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to do it is that the patient lies down on his back, then holds the head of the penis and stretches it as much as the length of a pen, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and be careful of bleeding which happens often, and if it occurs, stop it with what stops bleeding, and care for the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly symptom of disease; some are benign and others are not, so you must carefully cut them out with a fine lancet, clean them all, then apply a cotton swab dipped in Egyptian ointment; treat it with Diafinicon ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul and pus-filled color, then you should use cautery on it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it out and if the ulcer has reached the penis and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove first the one that is inside; and when it has healed, cure the exterior part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you cure it together, the head of the penis is not assured and can be pierced, and a black and corrupt humor comes to its rod and the groin; then one must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then bind with a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding comes, moderate the lunar cautery in this way:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is useful for two conditions together: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then one must insert a reed of boxwood into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin on the head of the penis becomes dry (which happens to those who have not been circumcised), or there is a wound or abscess, then one must scrape it with a curved instrument, until the foreskin is loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is difficult to do, then one must scrape it with a spatula on both sides of the foreskin and the skin; then gently separate and place a fine linen cloth soaked in cold water over it, so that it does not become dry again.
de la circoncision	Thank you for providing additional context. Here's a revised translation of the entire sentence, taking into account the new information:
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a loosening of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work willingly and specifically for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision for their children because they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen that most masters and surgeons who perform circumcision around a Dale, and with force, and with a novaculum; the cautery avoids it because there are two layers, and perhaps one is cut and the other remains underneath.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they cover it up and the pain is doubled, and during the cleansing around the Dale, the tip of the member is not assured; and during the cleansing of the nail, the iron perhaps slips and ruins the work, and often times it results in a situation where there is no need for cleansing, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the cleansing performed with force on the entire line of the scar, I have found the benefit of this method, for the incisions made with force cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" all the time; but let the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and the first task is to make the child, if they pay attention, think that you are only tying the thread around the rod, and then cheer them up in every way possible; then place it upright between your hands and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the rod and blow or cough, and pull it up until the foreskin of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind it with a double thread, then bind it under the scrotum to another ligature; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the scrotum and pull the head of the rod; then let the pouch run and run, for this is the foreskin; and put powder on it and on top of the powder a piece of cloth glued with half a beaten egg mixed with rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two ends should be blunt and sharp, and the ends should be as wide as a thumb, equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the contents of the incision come out; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the place becomes an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, let it be until the abscess has settled, and carefully flay it; cut it as you can move it, and be careful near the groin area, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of hardened things with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply with the knife and it goes beyond, it will not harm; so cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	for urinary retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The holding of urine is due to blockage by a stone, congealed blood, pus, flesh rot, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone located in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend on their knees, place their feet on their back, stretch their belly over the back, and restrain the patient's stomach as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the passing of the stone above, thus releasing the urine; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form: made of thin and light silver, like bird feathers; and let the cane be a palm and a half long, and fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine withdrawal is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end to a piece of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; cut off the excess wool and push it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis backwards over the belly; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and have the patient feel it reach the empty place, unless the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread out along with all the wool piece, and the urine will follow the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and continue inserting the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and ease the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction has gathered there, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, then use an instrument called a "clepsedre", and this is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the location for inserting the medication stopper should be such that it effectively stops up the opening, allowing for the removal of moisture and insertion when necessary; and when you see your medicines being administered into the bladder, place the end of the irrigator in the moisture and pull the attached cord; by pulling the cord, you will draw out the moisture into the irrigator, and then strongly push the cord back in; the moisture will enter the irrigator, making its way to the bladder, which the patient will feel; and this is the subtle form of the enema used for irrigating the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker?) is higher up; and below is the bladder or the place where the urine falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you would use to fill the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread, and heat one side of the moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then gather the circle like a purse, and put in it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"from the stone" (I'm assuming this is a continuation of the previous translation, if not, please let me know)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with their medicines; and I have told the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work with incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and succinctly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and sand appears, and the patient burns his penis, and he urinates frequently, and then inflames; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it is moderate in young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the cure, one should first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, causing the stone to descend to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes come out a bit; then have him sit between your hands, prepared, and let his hands be beneath his thighs, allowing the bladder to completely tilt downwards; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in its place, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out upon touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is young, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult; and insert it into their rectum, searching for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, guiding it towards where you plan to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to lift the hips with their right hand, and with their left hand remove the skin that is under the hips in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula cutting edge, which is its shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it [the stone] is located between what is between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but to the left side of the anus; and it should be directly on the stone, and your hands should be always placed either at the anus or at the stone, and the incision should be such that it is wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the hand that is on the anus will cause it to come out easily without effort; and know that there are some stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to extract; and there are some that are smooth, similar to a hailstone, and round, whose emergence is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then for the one who has angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary to squeeze with tongs that are like a file at the tip, in order to tightly constrain the stone so that it does not shatter; or you insert underneath it an instrument with a narrow, curved tip; and if you cannot trick it out in this way, then widen the hole a little, and if the flesh splits, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first put the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then place it on top, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it needs to be spread, and a bigger wound needs to be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things can happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes out continuously because the wound cannot heal; yet still try to drain it, or break it up with tongs, as much as you can remove it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply a mixture of incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and place an oil-soaked cloth on top, either in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then turn the patient onto their side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then cure it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses or ulcers come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to happen without a leap with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder and make it rot; then raise the wound with water and oil and salt, and help it in every way you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all the hours that you care for it, you tie its two thighs together and gather the medicines at the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the conduit of the penis, and fixed there, and urine cannot come out; then use this remedy that I mentioned earlier, that you cut it many times, unless it is excused from cutting for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have proved this before.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron fork in the shape of..., with three sharp points fixed on a handle.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will come; then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken at once and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for some hindering factor, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision on the rod towards the stone between the two ties, then extract it and untie the tie, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (a euphemism for a woman's kidney or bladder stone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone becomes incarcerated in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and prohibited for three reasons: one is perhaps because the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled enough woman who will reveal herself to midwives, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps a woman knowledgeable in this art of hands cannot be found; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, therefore a deeper incision is required, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a very skilled midwife, and such are hard to find, and if you do not find one, then carefully choose a subtle trick; and present a wise cup before her in women's matters, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command in the examination of the stone; and look very closely if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the bottom and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then she must press it beneath her finger, and command her to insert her finger into the womb of the patient, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she should slowly move it from
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 so that you know the similarities in order to recognize the opening.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if blood flows, apply crushed vitriol to the area and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the tools with you that I mentioned in the extraction of stones from men to assist you in your task; and if blood flows, and it is due to a cut artery, put powder on the area and bind it with bandages and bandages, and do not resume this, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because the patient might die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the area has cooled, return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	This passage appears to refer to the treatment of an inguinal hernia (hernie carnouse) in a medical text from the 12th-13th century. Here's my line-by-line translation:
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor (syfac), which is under the skin of the groin, containing the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin that we have mentioned earlier; and this only happens when there is a lump.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin area, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes a bruise on the hips, and this moisture has many colors: either it is of a yellowish tinge, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this occurs more frequently; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is of a whitish aspect as we have said, then the abscess is round like the shape of an egg, and the hips do not appear, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very flesh, then the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and for this reason, one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the hips and the whitish aspect, then one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, then examine all the intruding square, by which its shape is in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the insertion, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we heal it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their strength and body's capacity; then lay them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths beneath them; then sit on their left, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the kidneys; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the kidneys lengthwise until just next to the pubis, and make your incision straight, dividing the skin of the kidneys up to the white fascia, and carefully dissect it according to your ability; then pierce the fat filled with water through a large hole, and extract all the water, and then put in your drain, and stretch the fat upward; and only touch the kidney with the scalpel; cut the entire costal cartilage of it carefully, for if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg white (possibly a reference to pus) jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the kidney; then bring together the two leaves of the kidney lining with one stitch, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg (peritoneum) corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie off the blood vessels that are suspended, in doubt of bleeding; then cut open the peritoneum along with the suspensory ligament and remove the diseased egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if pus has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; cut the other part similarly to how you did with the first, then wipe away the blood and put a wet woolen cloth soaked in oil of roses into the wound; and put another wet woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and place it on the two corners, and put folded cloths on top, and bind it up with a bandage that is in accordance with this shape.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and stuff them with loose wool in this manner and sew them at the girdle of the breeches, and let one of the ends hang down to the backside, and the other to the part of the thigh; and the other two ends on the two corners, and let all the binding be gathered together in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this ramification is cauerized with a cautery instead of an iron knife, and that is when you take a scalpel-like cautery, and cut the skin of the haunches, and heat it up as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce through this pus with the tip, and scrape it off with this heated subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in all ways that you can, until you become exhausted; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be cautious of excessive bleeding, and be careful of surgical cuts; and if any contrary thing happens, such as an abscess or bleeding or other things, then cure what is causing the problem, according to what has been said before.
