Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo the procedure due to its horror, then perform an incision, as I have told you. This means that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that the ramicanth aquosum is ready, make the patient sit on a raised seat. Then pierce the abscess in its lower part, wide enough for the entire spatula to fit. Make the hole large so that all the water can flow out. Then place cotton on the wound and bind it, leaving it open so that the remaining water can drain. Cure the wound until it heals. If the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the mouth of the wound, then insert a feather or instrument used for extracting water from hydropic patients, as described before; widen the opening of the wound and know that the water will return and gather after 6 months or thereabouts. Once it has gathered as before, the patient will pass their days in this way.
de l’aposteme des coions	of a perianal abscess
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the sectioning of this branch, there is fear in multiple ways, which is why it seems better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come about in the body, and also in the joints; and this is due to various reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is to be known that it comes from an acidic and watery superfluity, which is spread at the hips, or from a percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not find any pain, and yet it is a serious abscess; and perhaps it is a fearsome and hardened abscess, and of a fleshy color, and sometimes it comes from a rupture of an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to swelling of the artery, it can be known by the feeling of a hot abscess when you press it with your hands; and one should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is suffering from swelling of the vein can be recognized by its appearance when touched with the hands, and a cut can be made in this manner on it and on other parts of the body; first cut the skin of the scrotum, then pull up the swollen part, and draw out the white membrane, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the swelling has become hard with these new growths, then you must cut out the swelling and the skin; and if it is attached to the sheath or within the vessels, you must free all of that attachment and remove the skin in a circular manner.[Notes: Here, "sheath" refers to the membrane surrounding an organ. The sentence can also be translated as "if it adheres to the sheath or inside the veins", depending on the context.]
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is in the back, you must cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said. (referring to a cyst or tumor)
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of a perianal abscess
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is a swollen abscess enclosed by a swelling resembling a lump, with softening of the nearby flesh, and the patient moves roughly when they walk; and the treatment for this illness is as fearsome as the one mentioned before, but nonetheless we will tell you about its remedy, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the support for the loins below your hands, over all the vessels that are close to the penis, and stretch them with your hands, and extend them widely; then cut with a sharp knife along the vessels, wide across, until they are uncovered, and then skin from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle where there is double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and then tie it again to the other end; then cut straight through the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as you would any other wound that needs bandaging, so that some vessels remain that nourish one of the loins; for by this no harm will come, and if veins come to all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the loins completely; so that the urethra does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of an abscess.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the abscess or the extension on the belly in the side of the haunches, because of which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the hips; and this rupture is either from the abscess or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes: either from percussion, or from jumping, or from coughing, or from lifting heavy weights, and from similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the abscess are that it happens frequently, over a long time, and not suddenly; and the abscess is even on the surface down to the depth because the abscess pulls the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is a section of the syfic, that it brings about sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears different close to the skin, because of the exit of the intestines and flesh outside the syfic.[FACT CHECK REQUIRED]
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the membrane (cirbes) comes out with the intestines and gets stuck inside, causing great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.[FACT CHECK REQUIRED]
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron (surgical) treatments there is fear, therefore one must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of the procedure is that you instruct the patient to move his intestines into his hand within the wound, if he can push it back; then hold his neck between your hands, and lift his thighs; then stretch his belly upwards, and cut all the skin of the groin longways; then insert retractors made of hooks inside the wound as much as you need to open it, and make sure the holes are large enough for the entrails to exit; then dissect the membrane that is beneath the skin of the groin until the white membrane is completely exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into the part that follows the groin, in the space between the white membrane that is beneath the skin of the egg and the second membrane, and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second membrane; and then move your right hand inside the cavity of the groins, and stretch the white membrane upwards to your left hand, and lift the egg towards the wound; and instruct the assistant to lift the egg upwards, and untie what is tied behind it; and check with your fingers if any part of the intestines has been wrapped around the white membrane, and if you find anything, place it back inside the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the membrane, which is after the skin of the groin; then cut the edges that appear from the threads, until there are four threads left; then arrange them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the membrane, which is beneath the skin of the groins, with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the edges of the threads, and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels that nourish it can enter inside, to prevent abscesses from forming; and place again the ligature according to the first long ligature, and after these two ligatures leave a space in the membrane that is beneath the belly as large as the width of one finger; and after all the rest according to the circumference that the egg bears; then cut in the part that is beneath the skin of the groins, as much as necessary for the blood to flow and the bowel to swell, as we have said before; then apply wet wool to the wound, and place the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white pus-filled abscesses that we mentioned are cauterized after incision, out of doubt for spread of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For it happens many times, and leave the ligament until it breaks by itself; and if it delays in falling, then soak it with hot water, and apply what we have mentioned, until it breaks; then cure the wound with another cure, until it heals perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	This passage appears to refer to the treatment of an inguinal hernia (hernie carnouse) in a medical text from the 12th-13th century. Here's my line-by-line translation:
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as a branch that is entwined around a vine, in such a manner that you bind the vessels after the incision lightly underneath; then cut in the middle and cure the abscess with what works, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have mentioned, until it heals perfectly.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes a rupture occurs in the intestines, as we have mentioned, and the place is visible; and none of the intestines come down to the hips, and if any do come down, it is little, and it repairs itself every hour; but nonetheless if it remains too long in that state, then the wound or fistula grows, so much that the intestines come out; and this happens because of the extension of the fistula which is in the intestines, as we have said, for it becomes extended, then softened and swollen, and the place opens up and becomes visible; and the cure for this is by cautery, as we have mentioned before; but sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen part of the rupture to the width of three fingers; and then extract the fistula which is under the skin that has become attached; then take a rod and place it on the visible surface of the fistula; and press it deep into the stomach, then sew together the two visible surfaces of the fistula with the rod, and sew both sides; then remove the head of the rod and do not cut or stretch the fistula or any other thing, as I have made you know in the cure for the branch of the intestines; then cure it with the cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, clean and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syfic (bandage) is constricting and has no appearance in healing, and the cautery is more effective in this place and closer to a cure.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the fat within is softened and it is visible. And when one wants to heal it, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their stomach, and cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal it like other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the threads.
dou chastrement	of the surgery/treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that castration is prohibited in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; however, it is necessary for two reasons: one is so that the physician can give a knowledgeable response when asked about it and know how to perform the procedure; the other reason is that we often need to castrate certain animals to assist us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I therefore say that castration is performed in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method of castration that is done by pulling, we make the animal sit in hot water until the area around the genitals becomes soft and limp. Then, grasp them with your hand and pull on them until they are removed and you no longer feel resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of the surgical incision: you should mark the beast, and press the skin of the haunches with your left hand, then tie the suspenders, and cut each ovary with a single stroke, when you have thoroughly flayed them; and leave some pouch of the sack and the thin sack that is over the vessels; and this method of surgical incision is safer than one made by attraction, because in an attractive incision there may accidentally remain something of the testicles, due to which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditus is of two kinds for men: one way is that between the two haunches there appears as the shape of the nature of a woman, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it has above the groin like a rod and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away the swollen genitals and treat them like other wounds. In the second case, for males from whom urine squirts through the skin of the groin, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tetanus (tension muscle stiffness)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tumor is a swollen growth on the genital area, so unsightly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you bind the excess of the tumor to your hand or with bandages and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so as to avoid bleeding. Then treat it with other treatments until it heals. And for another growth that arises at the mouth of the vagina, apply it, and perhaps it will come out, and it resembles a cow's udder, and therefore ancient people called it "the cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary that you cut it (
de erratique	of erratics (rocks or stones that have been moved or deposited by natural forces)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 It is necessary to cut it (the sin), as we have said, in the manner of the "tentigine," and cure it until it is healed.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If abscesses are about to appear, they are sure to do so either on your fingers or in your armpits.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle syphilis and it is near the groin, hurry and proceed as follows: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back, legs spread apart; then fully stretch the two groins so that the subtle syphilis becomes taut and is above the abscesses; then take wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the spot, and have the woman lie with a man each day, so that it does not stick together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the stoppings are of fleshy nature, then suspend it by a thread and cut it; and have ready hemostatic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then prepare a wide reed tube, so that the wound does not close up; and let it be like this for a while, and provide a linen tent; then let other wounds be treated until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when fleshy growth comes in the wound, then it should be covered in this way, if it is not inflamed abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an inflamed abscess in the wound, one should not use cautery.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they become swollen; and we have previously mentioned their likenesses, and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and swellings, when they are inside the anus and not noticeable to touch, cannot be cured by surgery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those that are at the opening of the anus, and can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you must place the woman in a cool house, then hold the swelling with pincers and cut it at its roots, then apply restraining medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then have her stand near the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and eggs, and make a plaster to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if he constricts (
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 And if not, apply cupping glasses to his back and breasts without drawing blood; then take wool, soak it in a solution of plantain juice or comfrey with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess is at rest, cure the area with a salve until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and similar to a rough surface, if so, cover it as I have said with a compress; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscesses come to the marris (?), such as chancre and hard abscesses, herpes, ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is thus necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marris, which is not one of the abscesses that swell bow-shaped; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is pointed at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not rush to pierce, but let it mature until the pain is eased; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small stools for them to recline on, and support their back and bring their legs inward towards the outside of the leg; and let their thighs be spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, and bind them well with a good ligament; then give them a bolster on their right side, and prepare the instrument that is used to open the maris, from which follows the procedure; and it is necessary when you wish to prepare this instrument, that you insert the rod first to know the depth of the maris, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the maris with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm them; and it is necessary to place the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and it is lanced by hand, you should cover it with a warm, wet sponge; and once the pus has drained, you should place damp bandages in the wound soaked in rose oil or dry, green oil; and place the bandage deep into the wound at the bottom of the abscess, and then place a clean, wet linen cloth on top of the abscess and wound; afterwards, treat it with appropriate ointments for 2 days until healed; and sometimes raise the abscess and wound with an enema of water and honey, and then with water or cooked lily roots and aristolochia longa; and then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is located on the groin, one should be careful not to cauterize with iron, but rather treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the shape of a natural childbirth, and one sign is when you see the woman pressing downwards and having a desire to smell something; then the child hastens to come out; therefore, know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the birth passage is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, gently press on her stomach so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth will come with it, and the groin will be cleared of its impurities by a good cleansing; and one who comes out differently does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 For it happens sometimes that he comes to his feet, and the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or often, and is turned by chance on his neck, and in other bad figures; so it is necessary for the balancer (scale operator?) to be wise and skillful in these things, and to watch out for error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out headfirst in a natural birth, and the woman is having a difficult time, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be held by other women. Anoint her privates with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place the small spatula-shaped instrument (the form of which is shown below) between the midwife's fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 and split the ligature, and cut at his nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must give an enema to the woman of fenugreek with oil of Saint John's wort; then make her drink a concoction and sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if both arms dislocate, you should gently and frequently relocate them; and if they cannot go back in, have the woman sit on a seat, and lift her legs up; then turn the seat upright on the ground, and make sure she doesn't fall when standing up; and if the arms still can't go back in, and the child is dead, cut the child's hands with the knife that is placed here, and extract the child, and likewise relocate (the arms).
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's delivery on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on its feet, you should lift it up; and then gently turn it from side to side until it is even; then take hold of its legs and stretch them gently from side to side.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If he can jump up to his knees, order him to take a deep breath and make him sneeze; if he jumps up, so be it, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not stay (in place) as we have said, then twist and turn it repeatedly until it matches its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will stay in place easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant. de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	with the baby's arrival on her knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, place the valve's hands beneath its buttocks; then support its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; fold its hands beneath its abdomen, and then take hold of its hands and place them on its belly, and remove its diapers from underneath, so that it is prepared below; and if the child does not urinate, take its feet and move them vigorously, then move its belly upwards, and insert your hands; and rock the child gently; and tell the woman to pull up as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the infant who comes out with one hand at a time
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to use a trick to reset the hand: if it cannot be reset, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the bed, and strongly push her legs apart; then prepare the instrument as I have described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, and then study how to reset the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and tell her to pull up as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's exit on its neck, and have her spread her hands and turn her face toward the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary for the surgeon to take hold of his hand, then turn it back and forth lightly; and when they are even, place a piece of lard and oil on it, as we have said; then instruct them to move it back and forth; and once you have done this, make them sit up straight and tell them to take a deep breath; and make them sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all veins.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out in this manner (i.e., after making the patient sneeze) with all the mucus, cut the suture at your nail as far as the moisture has been evacuated; and if the infant hangs on its face and neck, cut it from the womb so that it is not retained, and the infant will die; then put the child back in, making sure to place it correctly, and instruct the woman to take a deep breath; and it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth canal of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four at once; and this is not something strange, it does not happen very often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things, and do not live long, unless they are named; I know what they are, that they may multiply, and are separated by the umbilical cord which divides them, which is attached to the belly; and sometimes they come out naturally like lumps, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out forcefully, so treat as we have said, and let the balancer be skillful, and do quickly and lightly what he does; and do it in such a way that it benefits movement towards healing.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb as I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise one, and it is necessary that the balancer knows this, because by chance similar things happen; and do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child[translated from French to English by me, Adina]
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure the woman of a dead child or swollen belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be placed on her back, and let her hips be inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and let the minister attend to her from two sides, so that she is tied to the bed so that she cannot be disturbed during the delivery of the child; then anoint the mouth of the uterus with moist oils mixed with musk, althea, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then anoint the balancer's hands with these oils and musk; then insert them gently into the woman, then look for a suitable place where the navel cord can be tied, and take care that the child is positioned so that it can descend on its head; then tie the navel cord to one of its eyes or neck or mouth or soft palate or under the beard or in the cheek or near the ribs or at the middle of the chest; and if the delivery is at the feet, then tie it to a finger and the middle of the chest; and it is necessary for him to hold the navel cord with his right hand, and place the basin between his two hands with his left hand, and insert it gently into one of the places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the navel cord:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 then place another bandage across it, or a third if necessary, so that the traction is even; and then stretch it evenly, moving it back and forth, so that the muscles can exit, and make sure the bandages are tight to hold the muscles in place, as shown in the following illustration:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if some of it remains, have the patient anoint one of his fingers with oil and insert it into that part, while pulling the other part; and if there is still some left, place the bandage higher up and continue to do so until it has all come out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back through tightening, you should wrap it in a cloth until it has all come out; then bind it at the joint of the wrist or ankle, and do the same with the other hand and both feet.[`html(<br />`)`]
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and tight at the opening, or if it has a swollen forehead, then you should insert the sharp-pointed spatula between your fingers and make an incision in the forehead to drain the fluid; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," with which the shape is formed along with the other instruments or chapter that comes after this one. And do the same if the child has a naturally large head; then pull out the bones using pincers, and if the head comes out forcefully and is constricted by the "forcele," then make a hole in it until the fluid in the swollen area drains out. And if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if the belly or below the ribs are swollen, then you should pierce it until the fluid runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is standing on its feet, the drawing up is easy, and the leading to the mouth of the swollen area is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is constipated in the belly or breast, it should be extracted with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and open the belly or breast, until the moisture that is there runs out; and if the other members are removed and the excrement remains, then the physician should put his hand deep into the anus, and pull it out up to the opening of the anus; then insert one or two fingers, and pull it outside; and if the opening of the anus is narrow due to a hot abscess that has come there, then it should not be manipulated, instead moist and greasy things should be applied; and apply soothing and softening plasters, and place it in warm and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side and you can straighten it out, moderate what we have said in "the living child"; and if there is no power to do so, draw it out in pieces and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And once you have done that, moderate what we have said in abscesses that come in the groin; and if bleeding comes, it should be placed in restricting water, and moderated with other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had died and then a second one was sewn onto it, but the second one was not dead. (my attempt at a translation)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her belly and it became so swollen that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly. (my attempt at a translation)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, and was unable to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and there came out a bone, and after several days, another one did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for the belly has no bones.[Original text uses "ventre" to refer to the abdomen or stomach area.]
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	And so I thought that it must have been the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I treated the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time like this, and frequently passed wind from the wound; and I only recorded this chapter because, when the master finds a foreign object, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the fracture to its proper position
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, which can be found in books; and it has two levers at the two sides of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nonetheless, let the horns of the restrainer be finer, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the bow be two fingers wide, and the edges of the branches one palm and a half long; and in the middle of the two limbs there should be two joints of this same wood, which are fastened in both, being half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the bow to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, in the shape of pincers; and let there be two joints at the two ends, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the bow with the entire instrument, place the woman on a bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two joints adjusted together in the bow, and hold the head of the instrument beneath her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument, just as you did with the pincers equally, according to the width that you wish to open the bow of the instrument, until the ball does what it is supposed to do.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharpened and have many variations in their forms. And when the surgeon has prepared them, he works more quickly, with greater force on the incision, because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain using the instrument once it has been prepared, for its necessity is not to be scorned.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with some aid, and restrain her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she faints from this, it's all right.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot, and make a hole in its cover, and put inside herbs that can open the womb, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over fire; then place a reed or hole of the pot on it, and the other end in the mouth of the womb, and keep it there until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sinews pull quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and does not go away, order the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or musk gel of aloe, and then put it on the wound, and seek out the second intention; and when she has found it, so take it and stretch it slightly and directly, so that the sore does not tear during the extraction; but it should be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and dry up.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the sore is very tight, we have said the cure is to make it sneeze and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not go away after all that we have said, make sure not to force during the pulling; but it is necessary for whoever is at the mouth of the sore to tie it to the thigh of the woman, then enema her with theriac ointment; it will soften and restore it, and it will come out; but nonetheless, when it softens, an unpleasant odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is necessary to use appropriate fumigations for that: some of the ancients have proven fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained menses and after childbirth is as follows:[translating instructions for an instrument for fumigation, not given in full here]
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like a hedgehog, and the head is gently placed in the natural position, and the limbs are stretched out over the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the procedure continued until the procedure is completed, and another one begun.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament[ (i.e., anus)](Note: This refers to a medical procedure for treating conditions such as constipation or hemorrhoids.)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have a perforated anus, but instead have it stopped up by a thin membrane: therefore, the midwife must pierce this membrane to the right side, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, taking care that it does not touch the lancing; then place wet wool soaked in wine and oil on it, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will suppurate, put a piece of wood into the wound, and leave it in for several days, and have it removed when the child wants to go to the chamber (toilet).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages (clots) come from a sudden wound or abscess; such a stoppage must be covered and treated as we have said with the piece of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus/rectum.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the buttocks are swelling and growing near the buttock, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still has whitish moisture or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that something comes out or windiness when the patient makes an evacuation, and perhaps in his jump a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and to the groin.[Note: I translated "nout" as "groin", but it could also be translated as "buttock"]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And so one recognizes the persistent fistula of the buttocks, and not persistent: it is done by inserting your index finger into the buttocks, and inserting a thin needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is curvature, insert a slender tent of lead or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no egestion or ventosity comes out of the wound as we have said: know that it has not pierced; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the urethra, if the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it pierces as far as the joint of the thigh, the tent reaches to the location; if there is no curvature and no finding of pain around it, then it is that it will always be bent, and neither medicine nor surgery through ointment is of value; and in these perforated fistulas, there is no cure except for labor, and foolishness of false doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one who is not persan nor ancient, there is hope of health through cure by fire, as I have tested, and it is that the patient lies in your hands on their back; and lift the legs up to the thighs, and have the thighs inclined towards the belly; then insert a tent stake of iron, or of wood if there is curvature, until you know where the stake comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the rectum, you should insert your index finger, and if you then feel that the stake has penetrated; and uncover the area where you feel between your finger the abscess or flesh, then know that it is persistent; and do not work further for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Always bear in mind that one can indeed cure certain individuals, but it happens rarely; and the aid we provide consists of heating the cautery gently according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and then inserting it, still hot, into the fistula until it reaches the base. Repeat this two or three times, until you are sure that the damaged cartilages, which resemble a bird's feather, have burned away. Then cure it with moist bandages smeared with butter, until the damaged cartilage comes out; finally, cure it with a healing ointment that promotes tissue growth and heals wounds.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If this (condition) cannot be healed otherwise; and if it swells and does not burst until it reaches the finger that is at the base, and between your finger and the swelling there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue, and you see the fistula following the covering of the tumor; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the swelling forward with the incision, and cauterize it until you reach the tip of the swelling; and the swelling will be released and will fall off; then clean away the decayed flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overpowers you and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or a medicinal styptic.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning of gathered flesh, and the staunching of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of swellings moistened with butter or pounded herbs, until the place softens and the burned flesh comes out in the softened area; then the wound is treated with binding medicines that cause hardening.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is removed from the body, place your finger in it and feel around.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the abscess, and between two is the cloth or syringe or probe, which is close to piercing, let there be nothing but a way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if you can, place tents and care for it as before; and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and excretions come out unintentionally; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut next to the foundation, either with a tent or with another pointed instrument; then clean the cavity that is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound, and to maintain the fistula on the outside of the foundation: it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are formed in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula and it is next to the foundation near the skin above, then take a probe with a pierced tip of this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted thread through (the hole in) the two (prongs), and push the tent peg all the way to the end of the fistula, up to the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it [the probe] is pierced at the margin of the foundation inside, then draw the thread from this hole, as if you were inserting your finger into the foundation; and pull the head of the thread and bring the two sides together, and hold them close to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the threads cut through the flesh between them, and become detached; then cure the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one should not make an incision so deep for the sake of letting it drain and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.[NOTE]: The previous sentence suggests that making a deep incision to drain a wound or infection can sometimes be avoided by using other methods.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spatalon spine that is used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
