The one that is born in one of the knuckles of the finger does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the size of the one that is fleshy is small, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold him with forceps.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one that is born in the back of the last knuckle, you must first cut the flesh roundly until you reach the bone, then cut the bone to an appropriate size, then cure it until it heals.[It is important to note that translations are not always straightforward and may require contextual knowledge or interpretation. The above translations aim to convey the meaning of the original text as closely as possible while using modern English.]
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The unions that come together in the fingers can occur by birth, or by healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 It is necessary that you cut that suture, so that the (body) parts can return to their natural shape; then place between two tentes or damp cloths wet in rose oil, so that they do not join again; or you place between two thin pieces of wood, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of these with the palm, then cut open that swelling as is necessary.
des vils	 of vulgar things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large, swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to them at times, and then treat them with basilicum (a type of medicine).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron is of two kinds: one is to cut and let out the black blood; and the other kind is that you raise the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this manner: first make the leg very hot with strong water, until the thick vein becomes thinner, then squeeze the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bind it up, and tell him to eat foods that cause black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and this will harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The treatment is as follows: raise the patient's leg if there is a lot of hair, then place them in a bath and apply warm water to the leg until it turns red and the veins become swollen; and if you don't have a bath, heat it by the fire. Then make a cut along the vein at the top of the knee or below the ankle; then lift the skin with a lancet and cut the vein from both sides until it is visible when touched; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord. Then insert a probe underneath until it is raised above the skin, then gently pull on the lancet, then make another incision next to it in three places; then lift the skin above the vein until it is visible, then lift it with a probe as you did before, and attach it to another lancet as you did first. Then make another cut or several if necessary, then lift it and attach it to the toe of the foot, then pull and lift it up to the second cut; then remove it from cut to cut until it is completely removed, then attach it. And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a needle with strong double thread and tie and pull it, and insert it underneath a probe, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; and make sure it does not tear, because if it tears, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and this will harm the patient. And when you have completely removed it, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye sight is constricted and twisted and rolled up together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron with which you cut the eye should be curved and not straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it should be of thick curvature, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein runs in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth that has no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to decay that comes from under the skin, as a snake or worm crawls inside the body, running between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this illness are that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then the location changes and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the vein is open, you should wrap it with a piece of linen about one and a half to two fingers wide, and bind it, leaving the linen hanging from the leg. And every time it protrudes too much, wrap it again with the linen and bind it. If it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the rest, but do not cut it at the root until it has fully come out. For if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause abscess and putrefaction at that location, leading to a serious illness. Therefore, it should be treated little by little until nothing remains in the body. And this vein, when it is treated, can sometimes be five or ten palms long, and a man came to me once whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, insert one finger's width or a hole and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out. Empty the contents inside and apply healing medicine to the location for several days, then treat it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, many runners, and even when it appears in the joint of the foot, or the foot, and there comes a lot of pus, and then it heals; cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "maladie de buef" (ox disease) in our land, because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down, and one can feel its movement from member to member, as it causes the skin to break open and burst; and it comes from the putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, serpents, tapeworms, and ascariasis in the stomach; and there is fear for its harm, because when it travels through the body and goes up to the head, and reaches the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled, it cannot be done without it going: therefore, you must then tie the place above and below with a strong ligament very tightly, then cut and pull it out, and if the wound goes deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it can do is to make the eye run, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, pull down the eyebrow very strongly, then cut and pull it out; and you must use the patient with purification of the body by resolvent medicines for the bad humors, and be on guard against putrefactive foods, so that putrefaction does not occur.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain coming from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it move up to the shoulder, more quickly than any other thing, like quicksilver when it runs from place to place; the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and then soon spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it turned around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved in this way, from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease exhibited in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nevertheless, I have often seen that
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this disease being treated and the patient feels pain, if they reveal it to you as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then cut it open until that constrained flatulence comes out; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with those who unblock flatulence, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of them (arrows) are such that there are some with large points, and small ones, and feathered, and barbed; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and an arrow that falls in a limb does so in two ways: either it stays in the principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it (the arrow) falls in one of the places in these limbs and the signs of death that I will tell you appear, then you must be careful in extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain lifts up, is when there is scotoma (a visual field defect), stiffness, dizziness, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge of fluid from the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there is a flow of clear fluid from the wound appearing like small pieces of flesh, and also foam coming out of the wound; and if these signs appear, then you should refrain from treating it, and pull out the arrow if it is not deep within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow when it falls near the left breast are that it feels close to the left breast and also as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow twitches like a beating heart, and produces black blood, and comes chills and cold sweats, and fainting: know without doubt then that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has hit a vital organ is that pure foam spouts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color and sighs deeply, seeking cool air.[Instructions for this task:
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the covering of the chest, it is near the ribs; and it causes great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some undigested matter may exit the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrows fall on the belly, and it comes out any feces through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrows fall in the bladder, and urine comes out and it becomes external, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is deadly.[INTERRUPT] I apologize for the error in my previous response. The correct translation for "Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules." is:
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions. Here is a more precise line-by-line translation:
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that which happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened that an arrow fell on a man's cheek near the root of his nose: I extracted it and pulled it from the other side under the ear fat, and it was healed without infection.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And I extracted an arrow that fell in the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrowhead was buried, and I could not reach it except for its point, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the wound healed, and no ill befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pull an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears: I saw the bristles, and subtlely pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And pull an arrow from a man, who had it fallen in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition had not changed. I cut around the arrow, and extracted it by means of a tool, and pulled it out without any bad consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound has healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not affect his natural condition, nor does it cause any problems with his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And I saw another man, to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was healed; and he remained without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen in the middle of his nose, and was slightly slanted towards the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded. I was called to the cure after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.[ Schlomo Pines and Tzvi Langermann in "Medical and Para-medical Texts from the Taylor-Schechter Genizah Collections" translated this as "I inserted a delicate probe, without feeling anything; he, however, experienced sharp pain and discomfort below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster of atrative and digestive powders on the spot because the area did not swell; and the spot where the arrow was appeared.[ Schlomo Pines and Tzvi Langermann in "Medical and Para-medical Texts from the Taylor-Schechter Genizah Collections" translated this as "I surmised that it might have been the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster made of atrative and digestive substances, for fear of inflammation; and lo and behold, the spot where the arrow lay became visible."](Note: The translation of medical terms can be tricky, as they may have different meanings in modern medicine, but here 'atratifet' is believed to refer to a substance that draws out foreign objects or pus, and 'digestif' refers to substances that help break down and remove foreign matter.)
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrow that was lodged in place; then I introduced the corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible; and more than four months had passed when the wound began to heal, such that I inserted forceps, from one side and the other, but they could not exit; so I did not cease in my attempts and efforts with various instruments, until one day I took hold of it with well-made forceps, according to its shape as will be described at the end of this chapter, and pulled it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons deemed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of extracting some arrows, so that you may apply your efforts to what I do not mention, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters compare even small things well, and find a remedy for what is present and lacking in the handling of unusual occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit the members in which they are embedded except in two ways: either by the way they entered, or by another part; and the one that exits where it entered is an arrow that has penetrated fleshy parts and exits at times.[](Note: The second sentence could also be translated as "and the one that exits at the same place where it entered, this is an arrow that has penetrated the fleshy parts and exits sometimes.")
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and likewise if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, cut all around with a fine lance, until the hole around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull of the head, and goes as far as one of the membranes of the brain, and any of the symptoms that I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it be until it is even after several days, for if the arrow reaches the membrane, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow has only struck the bone without reaching the bladder, and the patient remains for several days without any adverse effects, then attempt to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer tenting around it as I have told you; then heal the wound until it is clean.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is embedded in the body and cannot be seen, search for it throughout the wound; and if you find it, then remove it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve or vein, then enlarge the wound until it is wide; and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears or anything else by which it is held, then cut away the flesh that is attached to it from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can remove it; take care not to break the arrow, so that you may remove it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out in one stroke, leave it there until the flesh has swelled around it, then pull it out, for the extraction will be made easier by this delay.[TECHNIQUE TRANSLATION]
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is against you, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use a device on how you can safely pull out the arrow, whether soon or later, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same condition that they were in when the arrow fell, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do so, then place them according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot if it can be seen or felt evidently: then cut there, as much as the pliers can reach, and then pull it out; but do not hesitate.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand circularly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, let it remain so, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if part of the arrow remains inside, push the whole shaft in; and if it has broken off, and you wish to administer a suppository, introduce the instrument with the tip first, so that the point of the arrow enters the instrument's hollow; and then pull out, and if the arrow is stuck, introduce the instrument with the tip entering first, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary to cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the foot or in the belly or in the bladder or on the side, and it is close by and can be covered, do so; and take care not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and stitch the wound if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is similar to a bird's feather, for driving into the tip of the arrow, as shown in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pliers for putting in and pulling out [is] as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of the veins that are bled, there are XXXI, of which there are XVI at the head, namely: II batans which are behind the ears, which are called the "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in II temples apparent; and II veins that are in II eyelids of II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the head of the nose; and the II tendons that are in the neck; and the II veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is located on the left side, and the common people call it "head vein"; the median is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "belly vein", and it is above the fascia, and it is the one that is bled, which is clearly visible on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is located under the arch of the forearm on the left side, and the second saphena which is in the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The sowing of veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrh and headaches; and the quality of the sowing, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a cord until two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head: then take them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, tie it off; then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein and cut the skin and the vein well two fingers' width of the incision, and let the blood flow until you see; then bind and tie it up until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worthwhile for old and solid headaches, customary ophthalmia, and watery eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as follows: and that is that the patient strains their neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feel the pulse below your finger, and then bind it with a bandage; then lift the flesh above the vein towards your index finger, and insert the lancet beneath, and lift the vein up, and the cup, as you have done with the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then untie the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have previously spoken of their treatment and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work requires a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and slanted, for the bone is close by, and there is a risk that the flame will break if it is fine.[NOTE: I am assuming "li saine" in this context refers to the angle or shape of the flame. If it means something else, please let me know and I can adjust my translation accordingly.]
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the inner canthus helps the eyes, and for lice, and for redness, and for swelling in the eye, and for facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting with some ligature, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be a little long and wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; so collect the blood and use as much as you need, then bind it with cotton and tie it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The sap of the vein in the nose is worthwhile for headache, and for sudden madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and similarly when it is old; and the quality of the sap is such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand, and take a thin, subtle flame, and stick it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The scarification of the two sinews helps with the constriction of the windlass, and the beginning of paralysis, and many diseases, and abscesses, and corrosion, and herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the scarification is such that the patient wrings his neck from one side to the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein widely but not too much, then draw blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then perform another incision in the other vein, then untie the ligature and gently constrict both veins, so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so that the wound dries.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow/discharge from the sides/flanks
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"Bleeding of the veins in the upper lips helps with colic in the mouth, and decaying gums, lip cracks, and nasal congestion or swelling." This sentence describes some of the positive effects of blood-letting from the veins located above the upper lips. It is said to alleviate colic symptoms in the mouth (possibly related to teething), as well as issues with gum health, lip cracks and nasal congestion or swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the discharge are as follows: make the patient sit in front of you and constrain their neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them: then stop/stanch both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then stop/stanch the largest one on each side; and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the discharge beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The flowing of blood from veins that are under the tongue aids after the bleeding of the cephalic one, and that is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeder are such that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein: then heal both and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins in the arm that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: by pricking with a large mirror-bright flame or with an olive-shaped, sharp point like a cutting lancet, which is called "anesil"; and they are large and sharp according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open veins filled with thick, visible blood, and which contain clotted blood; and this is the shape of an olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed at the tip, and is used for healing thin veins with thin, yellowish blood.[Comment: The word "citrin" means "lemon-colored". Here it probably refers to the yellow color of the blood in these veins][Comment: In this sentence, I translated "sainier" as "healing", but it could also be translated as "cleaning", because in medieval medicine, opening a vein was thought to clean or purge the body]
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are located below the throat, neck, chest, and stomach; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed carefully and be cautious of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery and a gush of blood comes out, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking but cutting smoothly like a lancet.[note] "anesil" is an old French term for a surgical lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, you should constrict it, and apply another one; or seek a branch of it, or heal the vein in place of it along the arm: it opens manifestly; and cover it with a damp cloth, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to know the location of the bleeding, you should proceed as follows: squeeze the arm and feel for the place until you detect the pulse; then mark the spot with ink, and bind the arm, and apply the cautery to the vein with a damp cloth; and be careful not to strike an artery when you see the swelling, for this is the artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it bulge up high, similar to a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if so, bind the arm and leave it like that, and do not move it, let the patient not move it either; and be cautious, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its origin will retract, and stop the blood flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel root, split it, and take one half of it and bind it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and stopping the bleeding is not difficult in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The wound in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the top of the head and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic vein, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful about the nerve that is beneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cure it with a silver instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The wound of the cephalic vein helps so that it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to cure by pricking with the olive-colored flame or the myrtle-colored flame, because this is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nonetheless, one should try to find the easiest approach, and not worry if it fails the first time, and one can try again; and perhaps the area swells for some men when it fails the first time, but they should not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanies (pus) is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not performed unless it is to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, faste, and basilic; and one should perform bloodletting at the beginning of prayer time, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be performed on the first or third day, two or three hours after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The liquid that is administered for ailments has no set time, but is given as needed day or night, at all hours and in every situation. And one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor pregnant women until the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old French text: Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when one wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary to cleanse the intestines with a light enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw superfluidities from the intestines causing harm to the principal members. Nor should one bleed those who are overly full of food, or intoxicated until they are sober, nor those who are edematous. And one should not bleed after a colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with women, work, staying up late, fasting, or great exertion that weakens the strength, either due to injury of the weapon or the body. Then refine the humors if the blood is thick by means of food and drink, and medicines if you have them. Then enter the bath if nothing prevents it, to further thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the worst arm above the middle, as we have said. And rest that day from labor, strain, lust, and similar things. And be joyful and happy, and let the one who is performing the bleeding lift their sleeves higher than the person being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature slightly in the middle, for if it is too tight or narrow, the blood will not flow. Then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt. Then moisten the bandage of the person performing the bleeding with a little old oil, then place their left hand on the vein below where they wish to bleed, so that the vein does not move and fail when struck by the lancet.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like strings in the flesh, and some are full of airiness, such that when one applies fire, they shrink back from the flame and cannot be opened, and it is thus with these; and if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the cutter must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, try again a little below or above that spot quickly, as long as the area is not swollen.[ST] Se il la voine ne puet ovrir, si est li leus trop enflez ou bien por ceu que la char et li poilz est desfait.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the wound is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him rest for one or two days and do not bind his arm: perhaps abscesses will form; and do not enter the bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small and you think that not enough blood will flow, then apply the flame directly into that opening; and perform the procedure quickly, so that the swelling subsides; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, but instead put a little bit of oil residue on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and the residue of the oil is beneficial in that location; and thus administer the oil residue in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the course of the blood; and do the same with triacle and bowel, when applied to the swollen area; so subtly the blood softens and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, even when it is only bled once, at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a wet sponge soaked in warm water and salt on the area, and hold it there for an hour; and you should do this after the issuing of blood from the vein, and if some black or green remains in the area after several days, it does not harm; and if you see it, put something made of aloe or myrrh dissolved in sage juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there comes an abscess and discharge at the basis of the shin: place then your hand upon it, and if you find a soft spot on compression of the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious not to apply any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps it may pierce the artery; but instead make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their strength and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the healthy and sturdy person, who needs bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide; and for the weak person, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by stabbing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for the person in whom the body requires bleeding, it is necessary to give damp bread in pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, let him be bled three or four times, and if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before bleeding damp bread in syrup made of mushed medlar, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chiches, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he has a wound, after the release of much blood, then it is necessary that he consume broth of meat, and fragrant subtil syrup, and make use of other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm, and purge himself another time, then it is necessary, when he has become weak due to heavy bleeding, that he bleeds drop by drop, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong veins, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.[NOTE: I assumed that "houres" is a typo of "heures". If not, please let me know.]
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to purge himself in another way, should do so on the second day or the third.[NOTE: I assumed that "d'autre part" refers to a different type of medical treatment. If it means something else, please let me know.]
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and causes fever; therefore, great quantity must be drawn out, and widen the opening until it reaches the size of a fingertip; then attend to all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on the wound when it bleeds, so that death does not come instead of clotting, and this happens many times when the one who attends is negligent; and it is not necessary, when you intend to unbind the arm and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, for you to press hard; nor if it is curved, that he quickly extends his arm, for that would be harmful; but allow it until it bleeds a second time; or you can apply the tip of a flame, until the congealed blood at the opening of the vein comes out, and then place a cloth soaked in warm water on top and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is compound.[
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is as follows: let the patient put his hand in warm water until the veins become red; then bind it gently so that the vein shows clearly; then bleed him across, not too much or too little; and make the incision large, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, return the hand to warm water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is used more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The sap of the willow tree of the right hand is worthwhile for all liver ailments, and this is how: strain the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein swells, if one sees it; and if the sap runs across (or astray), and if you wipe it completely off, it does no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are all bare without flesh underneath, and then return the hand to hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then put oil and wax on the vein to quickly heal it, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The flow of sap in the left hand is worth as much for the disease of gout, and does the same thing as I told you for the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The sap of the juniper is worthwhile for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the groin, and retention of fluids, and illness of the loins, and thighs and old legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his discharge are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from there over the foot go many streams; then bleed at the largest vein, either at the ankle or over the foot, whichever is more convenient.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you clean it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and clean it across as well, just like in cutting meat; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out, put the foot back in water and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the bleeding fails the first time, try again a little higher up, for the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the sole of the other foot as well.
