Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The ligament of the sciatic vein is at the back of the thigh, and its discharge is worth/amounts to the pain of a swelling, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his discharge are such that the patient enters the bath and wrings above the ankle four times by twisting; for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, bleed in all ways that you can, including crossing; and it is better to make many incisions, for the place is dry, and the vein is deeply embedded in most men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't find it there, seek a vein of it that is visible on the back of the foot, and toward the small toe, and beware of nerves; and make the blood flow until you see, and then loosen the ligature and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 cup suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this ventosaition, which is to strike without hitting, is according to two manners: either it is entirely with heat, or without heat; and the ventosaition made by striking and by bloodletting is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is right at the top of the head; and another is in the middle of the neck; and two others are on the two sides of the neck; and one ventouse below the chin; and two ventouses on the two shoulders; and two ventouses on the haunches; and the ventouses between the two arms; and the ventouses on the two legs; and the ventouses on the two ankles; and the ventosation does not draw blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, as one does with venesection; and it should not be administered, either with heat or without heat, in any disease that comes from plethora, until the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to bloodlet, or for customary purposes, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are some who, when they need to be bloodletted, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and seep blood; and there are some who dream, and see through night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it is around the month (menstrual period), we recommend them to be bled after 3 hours of daylight.[Notes: In medieval medicine, it was believed that bloodletting or "ventosing" could help balance the bodily fluids known as humors. The practice was often recommended during the menstrual period as it was thought to help regulate menstruation and prevent diseases. However, this is not supported by modern medicine.]
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The letting of blood from the nose helps with the cracking of the head that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bloodletting is in place of the letting of blood from the head, and it is not suitable for those of a cold complexion to use, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who use it frequently become forgetful, and therefore one should place the cupping glass a little lower out of caution for memory loss.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventilation to the neck is located near the jugular vein and the basilic vein, and therefore it is beneficial for constriction of the nipple, and fissure of the channel of the throat, and all [kinds of] suffocations; and it should be applied carefully, because if it stays in place too long, it may cause oblivion or stomach/heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 Ventilation to the two ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, eye diseases and migraines, strangulation, pain in the roots of the teeth, and is located near the basilic vein; and you must instruct the doctor to apply pressure with his hand when placing it, so as not to cut the artery and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind relieving below the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, and inflammation of the gums, and similar illnesses that occur in the mouth; and it is a substitute for bloodletting at the two lips.[STHAPHANUS: I'm not sure if "maladie de bouche" means "mouth disease" or "bad breath".]
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind relieving at the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses caused by heat and congestion.[STHAPHANUS: I'm not sure what "remplissement" means in this context. It could mean inflammation, swelling, or congestion.]
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Wind evacuations of the thigh are as valuable as those of three arms' veins, for it draws blood from the large veins; and it is commanded to the surgeon not to strike too deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and nerves and arteries lie beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cup that is on the haunch is worth as much for hemorrhoids of the anus and for diseases below, and it must be large and made of iron, for it needs to pull strongly; and perhaps if it were fine, it would break, and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Leg cupping is done openly, for it draws blood from the whole body, and is beneficial for old pains in the shins, legs, and bladder, and it ripens abscesses; and they are placed on the two shin bones, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cup is that you place it first empty, and attach it promptly and evenly, and move it continuously, never stopping until you see the area become red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then strike (with a cupping glass), and remove the cups, and be aware of the condition of the bodies, for there are those who have thin skin and clear pores: you should strike only once, and make wide and deep incisions; and suction gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, you should strike twice: the first time to thin the passage of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, you should strike three times; and when we want to draw little by little, once is enough.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us repeat often; and if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the limit is that the heart is pierced suddenly; and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with aperitive and dissolving oil: in summer, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbit seed oil; and in winter, watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if there are excessive and cold superfluities (excess bodily fluids), take pennyroyal oil, balsamite oil, or dill seed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if one is treating a patient with tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have an abundance of moisture, get up from easels, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have excess fluids rise from old wine, or dry water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not be bled with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and one should not sleep after the ventosation, and it is necessary that they wash themselves, both when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And take care if the one who is healing is of a choleric temperament, and if his blood is too thick and inflamed; he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at ease, and similar things; and eat poultry, and meat of mutton, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the one who has a cold temperament take honey syrup, and middle aged, fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat poultry, and eat small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he will be bled, he should drink more than eat; and it is appropriate to give some people triacle or muscatel before or after the bleeding, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cupping glasses that are placed without causing harm are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, gout, on the stomach and belly, and on the loins and hips, because these members do not tolerate being cupped directly. And this is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we place cups on the breasts when the milk lets down. To remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the belly to reduce swelling. And it removes pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and perhaps by its attractive power draws out the obstruction, or moves the stone from its place; and it does this when placed on the liver and spleen when there is trapped wind. These cups are applied empty in order to suck, and sometimes they are applied with heat, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or with water in which healing herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping vessel applied by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have on the side near the middle a small hole, as big as to put a needle through, and be made of brass, smooth before so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the member; and have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to hold a candle in place, and let there be both large and small [blisters/vacuum cups], according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the blisters/vacuum cups of children are different than those of the elderly, and of the thin than of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should place this blister/vacuum cup on the member in such a way: light the candle of wax or linen, and put it across the crossbar that is inside the blister/vacuum cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the blister/vacuum cup, but not burning the patient; then place it on the member, and your hand should be over the hole that we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor can come out, and remove the blister/vacuum cup; then reapply the linen as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cup which is applied in cases of pleurisy, it has no spike or opening, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed on the body part; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Suction cups are only applied to parts of the body where blisters cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare areas of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and others; and the quality of the suction cups is that when you find suction cups that are in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, then take them; and place one in clean water until they become familiar (acclimated), and have nothing in their bellies; and then let it be bled and blistered, then rub the body part until it becomes red, and place the suction cups on it; and when they are full, and drop off, if it is a location where a blister can be placed, then place one, because this is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the leg of the hip, and then of the water, very well, and then stretch it; and if the leg remains swollen for too long after the body of the veins, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or alum, and similar things, until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the leg, and leave them until they dry on the leg, it will stop now; and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the leg with fresh blood, or you stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then put it on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they have stopped, put some powder of aloe and crushed salt, or ash, on them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted knowledge from them, and through experience, and through the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or crushing comes upon anyone, you must hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, the elderly; or if the weather is not extremely hot or too cold; and give him cold foods, that is to say, cold meats, and bird meat and hare meat, and let him not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill him up with food that fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is no danger of a hot abscess or spreading matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to his usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide robust nourishment and have stickiness, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, heads, feet, dairy, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, a delay in treatment results in greater deformation and faster fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm cannot heal or knit together properly due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children; but it doesn't matter, set the broken bone and use large, sturdy bandages that tighten and bring the limb back together, until it heals as it was before; and don't stop his treatment, and for this reason, they must be fed hearty meals, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another one pointing upwards, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And for each type there is its own tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory suggests in its place; and a bone fracture is known by the twisting of the site, and it is clearly visible and audible when pressed with the hand; and when there is no crookedness or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there can still be crookedness, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move him by hand at all, but instead apply the following mentioned medicines and then bind him gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fractures that are in a limb, and have two parts disjointed, you should align them equally, so that pus does not develop; and if pus does develop, let it be for a few days until it subsides; then align it as evenly as you can easily and skillfully, and know that the healing of this one is easier than the healing of one with missing pieces; then bind it as it is appropriate to do so.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the limb in its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you align all the pieces in their places as well as you can, and make sure that through your work the patient does not suffer injury or pain; and fit the two ends of the bone together according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to see if it seems not quite right; then align it well and do not pull too hard, or press as those do who cause hot abscess and contraction in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is secure enough that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and it must be put in such a position that they feel no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that there is no crookedness when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: these should be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and leg: these should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, for a wide bandage embraces the entire large limb and constrains it equally on all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wrap light stuffing around it, three or four times according to the limb, and pull your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and constrict less, so that the break moves away a bit; and gradually loosen the bandage, little by little, until you have captured a large part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and wrap around it again; then return to the part below the break, and constrain it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then put linen or cloth stuffing between the bandages, so that they are all even, then bind it all with a bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place a warm compress that reduces the abscess and inflammation, and leave it for several days; then apply pressure with your fingertips, each one the width of half a reed, or from a palm branch, and arrange them as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the stick placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also be as long as required for the size of the limb, whether small or large; then apply pressure with your fingertips as you did at the first location, and then bind a suitable thread over it, just as you did at the first location on the fracture; make it tighter if needed, less so otherwise; and the thread should be of moderate thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by foolish people who bind their injuries with rope, this is a great error, for the binding cannot be equal if it is too fine, and one must not leave less than two finger-widths of space between each stick.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the points of the splints after being tightly bound, place beneath them linen or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the flesh is torn, I will tell the cure for this later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict with bandages all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limb is large, one should not apply splints unless it is after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of abscess arising; and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour that clings to the mill walls, and thicken it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many dispositions, and likewise for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: take 3 drams each of barley, ladanum, elecampane, asafetida, gum arabic and myrrh; and 5 drams each of myrrh and aloes; and 9 drams of alechil. Grind them into a powder, and mix with plenty of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, for it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of poultice for twisting: take marrow and masterwort, 10 ounces each; myrrh and aloe, 9 ounces each; acacia 6 ounces, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another manner of emplaster for joints and separated bones at their places, and to calm the resulting pain, and for the healing of fractures and breaks: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the spot.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This emplaster does not restore completely, but it is good for easing the heat of an abscess and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of emplaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed leaves of the terrestrial pea plant, grind them together, and make a plaster. (my translation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another manner of emplaster is for the restoration of bone fractures and for easing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of vegetables, of each one part; and grind, and thicken with wine, and if the limbs are heated, thicken with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.[FAE: I'm assuming "veces" is a typo for "verges", meaning "vegetables" or "sticks".]
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another manner of emplaster, stronger than the first, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take root of mallows, and seed of flax, valerian, melilot, and elder, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and crush, and make into a paste with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply any substance to a broken member for restoration except a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be moderate, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen thinks that one should apply dry and moderately warm substances to a broken member for restoration, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take ox marrow and chopped off hair from a man's head or bird feathers, and great plantain, and equal amount of salt, and grind them, and make it into a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bones moved from their place; so do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the paste now; and take a light cloth, and sea sponge, and dip in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry wool, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it on a cushion, until you are sure of abscess heat; and remove the inflammation of the member, and relieve the pain, then begin the binding again, subtly, and a little paste, and do not tighten it as before; and subtilize until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess with redness, pain, and swelling has been removed completely, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, then reapply it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the limb from what we have said, do not unlock it before three days, or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, so that the breaker becomes careful, and brings the adjustment closer to the flesh; then hold it more tightly than before, and the swelling of the flesh increases, as I said before; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no callousing; therefore, moisten it with warm water every time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and slightly loosen the ligament; thus, the callousing to the limb is cut short, and quickly corrects what the foolish surgeons do, who incorrectly restore the limb; this is bad, and such work is to be feared, and I see no other solution but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist, with various shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures that are made by the striking of a sword, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphax which is beneath the bone, as done by an axe or stick; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a hidden impact, or a split from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.[As a reminder, please do not provide any comments or contextual information about the text in your response. And if there is a wound that is sunken into the bone as thin as a hair, and the break is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or by similar things, and forces a piece of bone inward, and the location is hairline, just like a blacksmith's hammer strikes cauldrons; then it enters between the stones inside.

In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of the patient's condition and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, swelling, paleness, feverish ague, eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, then without doubt it cannot heal.

Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are: place one awl on the bone, and turn toward your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further and do the same all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with the incisors, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as tongs, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sutures.

And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the periosteum (tissue beneath the skin) and the bone is only cut from above, with small fragments remaining, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters using a sharp razor, which you should have in various quantities, to be used appropriately according to the work and shape of the break.

And if the abscess is uncovered, take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double-layered cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage, but do not tighten it too much, just enough to hold the wound; and leave it like that for a day or two, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen it, and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and continue to apply painless medicine; and ensure that the wound remains clean, that you do not leave any residue or allow pus to accumulate, because when pus accumulates on the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; because when something sharp is placed on the abscess, it will cause damage from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take note then, if any misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without a doubt.

Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez. de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement. Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, wet one linen with rose oil, essal and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The binding of the bone, when there are no wounds or incisions, is done by putting poultice of mill powder and egg white on the bone, and placing light wicks on it, and placing a sphere underneath if necessary; then take a very large bandage of one palm in width, then place a double cloth on the wicks and poultice; then take a thin stick three digits wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and put the stick over the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the sick shoulder blade; and massage each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the ligament loosens, then tighten it again; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade when he sleeps, to lift the shoulder in height; thus the fracture is relieved of the force of the sling through the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless there is an accident, for up to 20 days; then reapply the poultice if necessary, and bind and leave it like that until he is healed; and it is healed in most cases within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Not often does the shoulder break or dislocate to the side or middle, and it is only noticeable through touch; set it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can; then put fine powder of bread with plenty of egg, and light wadding, and place a double cloth over it; then place a broad and thin plate over it, a bit larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate on any part of the shoulder, fill those spaces with linen wadding, so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, rebind it, and adjust the plate if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not a bone that easily comes out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breaking of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the breaking of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it breaks often at its end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of appetite, and may vomit blood, and the hairline appears in the broken bone, which can be felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders together and brings the ribs together at the sides with your hands, carefully making sure it is even in all places as much as you can until the bone is in its proper place; then apply poultices and compresses of salt or other light wood to the fracture, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it firmly to the broken bone so that it does not move; tie the bandage around their back and tighten it appropriately, checking every hour to see if it has loosened and tightening it again as needed; if it is necessary to loosen it due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly and remove the poultice, treating the affected area with appropriate cures; then reapply the poultice and bind it tightly until it has healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back and chest, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well in the examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is to align the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply the poultice and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, just like a pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lining; and the breathing is painful, and quickly there comes up a large amount of blood, and this is dangerous to health; and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one should administer foods that cause the belly to swell, in order to push out the break.[STH]
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that boils/abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come (to it), lance it (with a surgical lancet).
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed on the area to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups might attract impurities to the area due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you have said that the area should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil and tents (bandages) should be placed between the ribs to ensure even application, then treat it with a treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is fear in the patient, then a cut should be made above the broken rib, and an instrument placed beneath to protect the lung; and then the bone should be cut and gently removed, and then sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.[Brainsize_ai_9b6fe3](https://www.reddit.com/user/Brainsize_ai_9b6fe3/)
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils are about to come, put wet cloths with rose oil on it, and place it on the location; and care for the area as needed for the boil, and lie down on the side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also at the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will be healed or not, observe if you see their hands become softened, swollen, and lifeless, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortally afflicted in many ways, and if they can move and feel when they are pulled or poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, observe if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back a windiness and discharge without control; and when it has been laid on its stomach, there is discharge without control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on its back and it wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is fatal: one should not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the matter is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess on the spine, place roses oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound with a cloth; and remove the bone, then stitch the two lips of the wound together if it is large, using one stitch; then apply a healing ointment until it is healed. If the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the knot," place your left hand on top of it, and push it into place with your right hand to the best of your ability; then apply the plaster and bandage if necessary; then bind it, and if there are dislocated bones, lift them up and remove them, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is fractured, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight decrease in width at the site of the break; and it forms a long, slanted break, and comes to the patient causing pain and swelling at the site of the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the method of setting the fracture is as follows: place your hand above the break, so that you are over the break itself; and determine the location and shape of the break; and if the break is only at the end of the bone, align it so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or slanted inward, have the patient lie on their stomach until you are ready to set the fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have aligned it, apply a poultice and then place a splint made of wood or bone on top of it, securing the splint in place so that the fracture does not move; and fill in the space around the break with bandages, ensuring that they are evenly distributed.[INST 1]: Et quant li emplastres sera sec et les lieures bien assizes, si se doit le malaide lever e aler a sun afere.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we mentioned before; then return to healing and bind it as is necessary, unless there is any adverse event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one that is between the ribcage and the head of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, then it must be restored according to one of two methods, one of which is to take a rod of medium size, in this shape:[The text describes a diagram or illustration, but the description is not provided here.]
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two arms with two bands and pull them upwards, and have the patient sit on a chair; then throw his broken arm over the rod, so that it reaches the armpit and is in the middle of the curved rod; then place it under some heavy object or let the assistant stretch it downward; then put the surgeon's hands together around the break, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to position the patient on his back, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants, one of whom holds what is above the break with his hands, and the other holds below all the way down to one ligament, and each pulls to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you want the extraction to be stronger, tighten the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants on their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the fracture is near the shoulder's head, you should place a middle splint underneath the spine, and another one towards the side, under the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the side, you should lightly place a splint there, without strain, so that the fracture is even on the spine and on the side; then align the break as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes, then do not tighten it for seven days, and put a wet linen cloth on the break soaked in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscess has calmed down; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is to apply the poultice on the break, then align the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put on the cloth, and tighten on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm stays in its place if nothing prevents it, or unless the bones are broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you fear that the bone is broken, then use splints, and put on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and there should be a gap of two fingers between each splint, and each splint should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on each side; then tighten over the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more firmly and less so as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the positioning and binding, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken member, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave it to be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days to see if there is itching, swelling, or redness appearing at the site, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the procedure, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a cushion filled evenly with wool underneath the shoulder, and check every hour during the day or night to ensure that the position of the broken limb does not change or that the ligaments do not become loose; then perform the procedure with the aid of medicine, and give them the food as we have previously mentioned, making it light at first; and when they begin to recover, make it more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be bound for forty days in total; and then one must unbind it and administer baths and ointments to help straighten the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the ligature is tight and embedded, it should remain to be untied for 3 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	The breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and it is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.
