When the small ribs are broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult, and it is more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small ribs are broken, then they should be lightly stretched and aligned properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large ribs, then they must be pulled more forcefully; and place a cushion under it, and hold the patient's shoulder higher than their other shoulders, and the small hand lower than the other hands, and have the patient lie crosswise on top of it, with the cushion raised higher than what the patient can bear. Then, extend the arms of the patient below, either to the part beneath or to a limb, while another person does the same above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the doctor sets it evenly, in the best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any piece that pricks the heart and cannot be restored to its place, then saw through it and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken about this in a separate chapter; then take care of it (attend to it).
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the treatment abscesses occur, place on them a compress of cerote made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and apply the compress gently until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the cerote and apply the plaster of flour powder with plenty of egg; place the stylets, and let the stylet of the breaker be stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or arms in multiple dispositions: either on one of the bones, or two; and pull more above the breaker than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages that are above the breaker be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is pulled be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And wrap the limb and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should moisten the limb with warm water until the itching is calmed down; and let the limb not be tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume tightening, and if the ligament is weakened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation does not come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it slightly and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation returns, and then bind it.[1]
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of the things that we have mentioned happen to the patient, then do not release (the limb) until after 20 days.[It's worth noting that the text uses "XX" to refer to the number 20, which was a common notation in Old French.]
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or within that time, then tie his hands to his neck, and make sure his collars are even, and beware of movement and loosening, and let him sleep on his back; and know that this break will be healed in 30 days or 35, and perhaps even in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but they usually result in bruising more often than breaking.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bruised, then the patient should sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them; then place their hand on a stretched out cloth, and have the assistant straighten the broken bones and align them properly until they are fitted together well; and apply a bandage and compresses, unless an abscess forms, then place a splint according to the size of the injury; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outer edge around the stomach of the palm, then make a sphere from cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their injured palm; then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the splint be made of wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, then place a splint on top of it, and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it around the entire hand, and fasten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, place it evenly as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit, place a straight small stake to raise the fracture and ensure it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together, making sure they are aligned, or place a stake on it, as with a splint; and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it is clearly visible when it twists in front and back; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each assistant extends their ligature evenly to their part; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And similarly if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be near the knee, and let there be extension downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bind it, if pustules do not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is applied in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary to wrap over the fracture a bandage folded double in two or three layers, and let the excess remain; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread upwards; then wrap around the leg and thigh the bandage, then place a stylet over the fracture, and place a stylet on the bone of the leg; then fill the gap with soft cloths to make the pressure even, then begin to tightly bind three or four turns on the fracture; and when it goes above the fracture, tighten it less; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you placed between the thigh and the leg, and tie three stitches that are above, then go down to the end of the thread until you come near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, if no abscess, swelling or any similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a symptom (such as an abscess or swelling), then loosen the bandage and address what has occurred, as we have said many times before. If there are pieces of bone protruding, then it is necessary to cut them away if possible; and if not, then it is necessary to break open the bandage and pull them out; and treat the wound as we have described, until it heals.[Additional context: This text is providing instructions for the care of a broken leg. The text advises that if there are any symptoms or complications (such as protruding bone), then the bandages should be loosened and the issue addressed. If pieces of bone are protruding, they should be removed if possible, and if not, then the bandage must be broken open to remove them. The wound should then be treated until it heals.]
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel is put in it, as in the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, in the restoration made this way, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 1 day, or a little less or a little more, according to the variations in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	This Old French phrase translates to "from the groin of the knee." The word "ruelle" refers to a narrow street or lane, but in medical texts like this one, it can be used to describe anatomical features. Here, it is being used as a term for the crease or fold of skin on the inner side of the knee, near the groin area.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the groin of the knee there is often a small break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a fissure or hole, and it happens in all wounds, with or without an open wound, and this is easy to feel.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put evenly what is dislocated at its two ends, until it can be moved as a whole; then apply the poultice, and place a round bandage if needed, and bind it as it is appropriate, then take care of all the arrangements as we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar ones; and put on each symptom what is necessary for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Here is the translation of the given Old French text into modern English, with the added context of "de la brisure de la jambe" (about the fracture of the leg):
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by its right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it breaks in the same way as the arm does, and for this reason, the restoration is also similar to that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones break together, the leg becomes deformed in all directions.[ preceded by a newline]
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, set them straight again.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it is clearly visible; and it turns blue.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension and align it evenly, and tie the bandages evenly as well. However, if the fracture is severe and there are multiple pieces, then the extension should be minimal and light; and adjust accordingly to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two straps made of wooden rods that encircle the leg on both sides, and extend from the knee to below; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and this is good. And some administer a long splint made of wood, and place the leg inside to prevent movement. This is done properly in cases where there is a wound; and move the leg daily to see if there is heat or any other symptom, and treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	And some administer a long splint made of wood for the fracture of the leg bones.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle is not prone to fractures, but sometimes the leg bones or two bones at the lower leg are broken in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see the bones protruding over one another, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on top of theirs, where the bones are protruding, then press down until they return to their place; then apply a plaster and bandages, and under the belly of the foot, place a small board with two flat chips, then bind it to the foot after you have wrapped drapery around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find the bones even, whether they be broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a pin in the broken toe according to the length of the toe, and it should be slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned, and bind it to the foot; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a pin according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the belly of the foot so that it is well supported.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I mentioned for other fractures, as we have said before; and treat each injury as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature (vulva) is broken, have her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support it from behind. Fill the hollow of her nature with cotton, making it as thick as your finger, then stand her up and lift her buttocks, causing the cotton to move in until it reaches the entrance of her nature, bringing the bone back into place. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton and replace it afterwards for seven days or so. The fracture will be healed. If desired, take a bladder from an animal, attach a cane to its opening, insert the entire bladder into her nature, then blow forcefully into the cane until the bladder inflates inside. Her nature will return to its original state, then fill it with cotton and leave it in place for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the arm in a man or woman is broken, you should reset it as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and such breaks are not hidden from one who applies their effort and skill, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a break indicates in several ways the correct path of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with cloths and leave it for three days or so, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, it is necessary that they be healed now, as the symptoms I have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply vitriol to it if you have none other thing, then immediately begin to reduce the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms, then delay the reduction for nine days until the abscess subsides and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad outcome.[ safer to wait until the abscess has healed before attempting to reduce the fracture.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin and is exposed, you must gently align it with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not ready for you to place evenly in your hands, then realign it with this instrument, which is made of iron, having 7 or 8 inches in length, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to press down on it with 3 or 4 fingers, according to what is needed in each fracture treatment; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb while you are working, and it should be sharp at the tip, and thick from the middle towards the front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," because the curved head should be placed on the visible end of the bone; and push it once, until it realigns, and make them even with each other.[Notes:In this context, palainche refers to a type of fracture where the ends of the broken bone are widely separated. The term "curved head" likely refers to the rounded end of the bone that has been dislocated or misaligned as a result of the break. The text instructs the healer to place this curved head back in its correct position, aligning it with the other end of the bone and making them even with each other.]
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is fine, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary for you to cut off the top of the bone, so that the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, such as an osteotome or a scalpel, to the best of your ability; then scrape away what remains in the bone that is rough and covered with small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is set back in place and the patient still feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Do so until it is in its natural position, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine and apply it properly if it's in the summer; and do not put any ointment or anything oily on the wound, as it may bring corruption; after setting the bone, administer celestial bodies (stars) and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; for many times have foolish surgeons done so, bringing death or corruption upon the patient; and let the constriction be gentler and softer than other fractures.[Note: I am not a medical professional, this translation is provided as-is without any guarantees of accuracy]
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or bad, and you suspect that evil accidents may occur, as we have said, and find pain in the place, then hard bandages should be wrapped around it instead of setons (small pieces of bandage or soft rubber used to attach a seton), and secured.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after 1 or 2 days that pus is forming on the wound, remove what you have placed on it and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrafarmacotion (a type of medicinal ointment) and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that the swelling can easily flow downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it can no longer heal but the swelling keeps returning, know that there are small bone fragments in it, for which you must stitch up the wound with sutures and remove all the displaced pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you should treat it according to what is said in its chapter earlier on.[It's worth noting that medieval medical texts often include references to "fistulas," which were seen as a common complication in wounds and abscesses. A fistula is an abnormal connection between an organ or blood vessel and the body surface, or between two organs.]
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out, for many die from this; but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days; then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that appear on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of the fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it is ugly to look at the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Pay attention then if the swelling comes to us after the healing of the fracture: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarcocollex, acacia, and similar things, either one of these or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg white or vinegar; and put it on the wound in bandages and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen it and start again, as many times as it takes to remove the nodules; or bind it tightly with a piece of wood, because the property of wood is that it removes all swelling from the limbs; and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess show; or have it shaved by a barber until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weakened limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and fragile afterward, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly; another reason is that there were too many bandages, preventing blood flow to the member; or due to excessive swelling; or from too much movement at the wrong time; or because the body has little blood, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make the body supple so that blood multiplies within it; and administer baths, and bring joy and pleasure to them; then apply poultices on the limb, such that the poultice draws a lot of blood to it, and often irrigate the area with warm water, until circulation returns to the member; and the member regains its natural appearance.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the crooked limb after being healed
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is crooked after being healed, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those who say that the limb should be broken again, as many foolish surgeons have done in our land; this practice is to be condemned, causing great harm, and possibly even death; however, if there are knots and tension, then they should be irrigated with warm water or softening herbs like those from the plant viscum album, including roots and melilotus; and make a softening plaster such as a well-made diachylon, take vinca leaves, infuse it in goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster with that; or use figs and pork lard, grind them up with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes a knot is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And move the limb slightly every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted parts (tortuositez) are swollen and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then one must cut it down to the bone using a sharp, light incision; and place cotton and bandages during treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by the displacement of a joint from its place, which prevents movement and results in deformity of the limb, causing the patient great pain and injury.[STH: Added missing word "caused" for better readability.]
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one waits, the place swells, and perhaps it cannot be put back in place; therefore, it is not good to move it when it is swollen: often this brings on spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient take a laxative, then leave him alone until the abscess has subsided; then soak the member with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw[ fem. noun, plural form: mandibules ]
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the jaw becomes dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly pulled out of place and become somewhat loose; or they become completely dislocated and hang towards the chin, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that the person cannot hold back, and they cannot close their mouth or enunciate clearly, as their tongue is trapped.  [Note: I made an educated guess for the word "envoloupe" which can mean either "wrapped" or "involved". Given the context, I chose "trapped"]
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is intact and complete, you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his small pillow (or cloth) with one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and let the other hand be free to align (or adjust); and command the patient to relax, his jaw, and move it in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician should make it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, soak them with hot water and oil, until you easily reset it; do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they (the jawbones) are evenly reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without strain, then place wet bandages dipped in a paste made of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two cushions so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor try to chew, but eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jawbones are healed; and then eat what you want lightly, and do not strain to open the mouth while eating and drinking, until the jawbones are well healed and cured.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly reset in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fever and swelling may result, and possibly stomach inflammation, and perhaps vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a lost cause; and many times those to whom it happens die within 9 days.
de la forcelle	of the fork (or pincher)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The "fork" cannot be dislodged from the side next to the ribs and the bladder, and it is sometimes dislodged out of place, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back, and extend their arms; then press firmly onto the joint with your palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the hip that is dislocated towards the leg cannot come out of place; if not, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, bring back the hip from the shoulder blade, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate in any other way than three manners: one of which is when it dislocates at the part of the socket beneath; and the second manner is at the part of the ribcage; and perhaps it dislocates at the upper part, but this happens rarely; and it never dislocates backwards towards the shoulder blade, nor does it dislocate inwards towards the nerves; and it often dislocates downwards towards the socket, especially for those who have little flesh, because it slips out quickly for them; for those who have enough flesh, it slips out with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they receive a shock or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.[Please note that "desaluee" in the provided text is not grammatically correct. It should be "desaloiée", which means "dislocated". I will use the correct form in my translation below.]
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you should try it, until you are certain; and only then should you begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocation is when it moves down towards the shoulder blade, making a clear distinction between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will find a noticeable difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade where you touch the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor make any movements; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly feel it; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place when it is recent, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant raises the patient's hand up high, then puts your feet under the pelvis, and pulls the joint with force up to the place; and the servant lifts the hand, and stretches it up, then puts it down; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said in a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and given soothing and relaxing remedies, such as a decoction of clover, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let them rest; then the patient should be propped up on their back, and place a soft woolen support below the shoulder blade, not too soft or too hard, then place the patient's heel on the support and lift the top of the shoulder forcefully, and pull the hand of the sick person; and another assistant holds the patient's head so that they do not move downward; this shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see that it is dislocated in this way: it is necessary that a person who is larger than the patient be present; and stand at their side, and push their shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and lift the shoulder upwards so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant pulls the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have him carry something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation is also reset in another way: by inserting a long stake into the ground, so that the head of the patient is as high as a fist, and neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but with soft blankets above; and have the patient lie down on the long stake; then extend his hand downward strongly, and the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it does not want to return despite all that we have said, perform this treatment: take a stake of two arms in length and four digits wide, with the tip rounded to enter deeply beneath the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place a soft cloth over the wood so that the wood does not injure the patient, then place it under the dislocation of the patient; and stretch the arm out along the length of the wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the arm at the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side; the joint will return in this way.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should then place underneath the dislocation a sphere of wool equal [in size], then apply ointment made with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it under the dislocation appropriately, and turn the binding over the ointment, and bring the hand to touch the neck, and let the hand remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats only liquids until the limb feels better, as it will heal faster; and then eat solid food after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised, then you should know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and you should know that the joint will never return to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is to the side of the hip, or the breasts, or the back, is caused by impact and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a replacement; and it should be treated until it has healed.[ original text was "i aministre on autre lieure" which I translated as "and another joint is used as a replacement". Other possible translation for this phrase could be "and an alternative method is applied"]
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes cracking in the limb and difficulty moving, then the patient should take many baths until the cracking has subsided and the limb returns to its normal state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been corrected, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the cut patient with the flesh, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it must be set in such a way that abscesses do not develop there, for if abscesses were to form there, setting it would be difficult and perhaps impossible to fully reset, especially when it is dislocated in the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, and more painful, and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, when it is of such a nature that it can be reset, is as follows: you stretch out your two hands and hold his arms spread wide, with the doctor's hands placed around the rib both above and below, pressing the joint back into place at its roots or the base of the palm until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the displaced joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and let two people hold and stretch the arm, so that it does not move during the extension; then bend the arm on both sides after you have wrapped a long and wide bandage around it; and when the surgeon has aligned the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns to its place; and when it is in place, apply dry ointment with egg yolk, and hold the arm tightly against the patient's neck, and leave it for several days before releasing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the binding and let it be; but if you see that the joint is not tightly bound, reapply the dressing and binding, and leave it for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels great pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and gently rub him, and press until he is relieved; or put sheep fat on the joint and leave it for a day and a night, then remove it and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint warmly, then replace the fat and then enter the bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung heated with butter and bind it on; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand has become dislocated, and the recovery is quicker than for other joints. Nevertheless, it should be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is thus: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and the doctor align it so that the palm is over the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns to its place. However, you must ensure that it is properly aligned; then let the patient place the back of his hand on the table during the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the doctor put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it (the dislocation) returns now, that is good. If not, bind it with soothing plasters for abscesses, and leave it like that without renewing (the bandages).
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot put it in place after several days, let the joint remain dislocated; and it will harm the patient only as long as his hand is swollen and he cannot grasp anything. Then know that the nerves or arteries are cut; and there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the injury, and perhaps that will be of no use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the emplaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.[Reader's note: The author is discussing the treatment of a dislocated finger or toe, suggesting to use an emplaster and then bind it in place for 5 days before removing the bandage. This is an example of medieval medical practices, where treatments were often based on observation and experience rather than scientific evidence.]
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is any cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and massage it until it heals.[Reader's note: The author is still discussing the treatment of a dislocated finger or toe. They suggest using warm water to help reduce stiffness and promote healing in case of any cracks or injuries.]
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then stretch out the finger, and push the dislocation towards its knuckles until it returns, then hold the finger's head and bend it towards the side where it is disjoined; and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently, until it becomes tight, and similarly do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and similarly do, when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the spine of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the swelling of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that stools come out involuntarily, unable to hold them back, and often some limbs become weakened, or both thighs or both arms or one, and often the hips move in four ways; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is to check if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancients have said that there are cures using grand words, but they are not always beneficial; I have abbreviated it according to my intention and created instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the front of the breast, there is no engine or health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one who comes specifically to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is stretched out on his face evenly, and has support beneath, so that he does not injure himself; then stick one stake in the ground deeply at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a ligament underneath the patient's ankles, and another at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants know the ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they are tightly fastened, the stakes as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine firmly, until it comes back to life.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms' length, and prop it under the affected area, and have the patient lie on his side, and place the head of the board under the affected area, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and have the doctor place his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it is necessary, do so with a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you drive two stakes into the patient's head, one arm's length apart, and two other stakes towards the feet, and have between each stake a palm's space in length; and have in each stake one hole, where the device turns, and have the stakes firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes have one turning stake, on which the ropes turn, and have two small stakes in each turning stake, one palm's length long, to turn the device; and then tie the rope that is between the asels to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other device, and each of the helpers turns his device along the entire rope, and the master aligns the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a dessicative plaster with an abundance of egg yolk on it, then the wool compresses, then an iron stake of three finger-lengths long, which reaches to the area of the gelatinous inflammation and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a ligature as we have said, and have the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if any complication arises at the end of the healing process, one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the iron stake that I mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes there appears on the back shoulder blade, and people think it is dislocation; but it is the bone that is visible, for which one should not make assumptions: perhaps it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints do not come out of place except for dislocations, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint can become dislocated in four ways: inwardly, outwardly, forward, and backward; and more so inwardly than otherwise, and slightly out of place in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee by the fire; and the place which is beside is swollen with abscess, because the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which is about to happen to him, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of that which is about to happen, is that he stretches his leg well according to its full length; nonetheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot advance, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he lifts himself up on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that which has already happened, is that he cannot stretch or bend his knee, and one leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the femur is located below the ribcage.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this type of dislocation is as follows: observe whether the dislocation is old and persists in its position, then there is no need for treatment and one should not be overconfident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, one should act quickly to return the joint to its place and stretch it both inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you should prepare and strongly hold the leg with two hands, or with a ligament tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under the heels, then gently tightens a soft ligament on the thigh; and another holds the end of the ligament; and they all pull up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four cases, and if the dislocation has been reduced as we have said, that is good.
