Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 Or if not, when the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto his healthy side, then place the ligament on the root of the thigh and the joint that is below the groin, then pull the ligament up towards the groin and the hip; then have another assistant take hold of the patient's arms and strongly embrace the swollen thigh of the affected leg, pulling it outwards; in this way it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot fasten it in this manner as we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligament at the heels and at the knees, and let the sick leg be extended two digits more than the other; then let him hang by a beam above his head, and let there be two arms' length from the ground; then command a minister to embrace the thigh's head, and let there be another minister hanging with the patient, who will strongly embrace the thigh, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten the ligament on the sick leg properly, and on the belly as well; then put two splints, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape; and have a cloth dampened placed around it, so that it does not wound the patient, then let each minister stretch out towards him, and let the doctor place evenly with his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on [a] board and press it as we have said in gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front [of the body], one must quickly stretch out the affected leg as I have said; and the doctor should take care to be over the bad groin, then press with his other hand and pull downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is on the outside, it should not be stretched downwards, nor lifted up from the ground. Instead, the patient should be positioned as if an abscess were present on the outside, as we have said in regards to lying on two abscesses; and let him be on his back, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and pressure should be applied to the joint on the board. And it will be sufficient when the patient extends his legs and they are even. Then, adjust the hips, and apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the abscess does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandages and apply the plaster again. And if you see that they are even, bind them as before, and leave it on for three days; then loosen the bandages and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee becomes dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and backward; but never in front.[Note: Dislocation of the knee in the front is anatomically impossible]
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not reach his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another minister extends his foot, so that the knee comes to its place, and the sign is that he easily bends his leg at his hip; and apply the poultice, and heat the leg against the hip, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then loosen; and the patient does not exert himself to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not aligned, stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely misaligned, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen and points to the side where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when moved slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold them by the leg above the ankle with both hands; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards and place the foot in its proper position; do this twice, as we have said, pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns to its place, that is good; if not, start again, for it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs and tie cloth around it so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one hand, and another minister holds the healthy leg below with their hands or with a strap tied around the shin; then stretch both legs equally, and make sure the stake is firmly between the patient's thighs to hold them in place when you stretch; then place the dislocated part in your hands and another minister holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot, you should make the patient sit upright on a level surface or table, and place your foot on the visible part of the joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is even, and there is nothing apparent, place a two-chambered plate under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly, and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the swollen inflammation, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the swelling does not increase; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing remedies for the swollen inflammation, and treat the wound as it befits, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are separated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and body.
Amen	 Amen
